Japanese Military and Political Authorities Plan for Self-Sufficiency in Oil and Iron, and Cooperate with Financial Circles to Develop 19

(Tokyo) The Army, Navy, Ministry of Commerce and Industry, Ministry of Foreign Affairs, and Ministry of Colonial Affairs have been considering setting up an organization to develop overseas fuel resources. Now, Mitsui, Mitsubishi, Sumitomo, and other companies are willing to jointly invest 5 million yuan as capital to establish the national policy of fuel. The company will be named Kyowa Mining Co., Ltd. A founding general meeting was held on the 1st of this month to decide on various clauses. When the company officially starts its business in the future, it will need at least 10 million yuan in capital. Currently, it plans to temporarily develop oil fields in the South Seas, Java, Sumatra, and Borneo. Therefore, Borneo Oil Co., Ltd. (capitalized at 1.5 million yuan), which is jointly funded by Mitsui & Co. and Japan Oil Co., will also be merged into the newly established company recently. The technical aspects and trial operations will be assisted by Japan Oil Co. to the best of its ability. Hashimoto Keizaburo, director of Japan Oil Co., said he will be appointed as an advisor to the company. (Domei News Agency, 4th)

(Tokyo) The special parliament has already closed. As the first step in the Hirota Cabinet's active industrial policy, Commerce and Industry Minister Ogawa said at this parliament that the two major national policies of steelmaking and fuel are aiming for a general parliament and attempting to establish it. Therefore, he ordered the relevant authorities to prepare as soon as possible the necessary investigation and research. However, on steelmaking, a general collection of basic investigation materials has gradually been gathered this time. Therefore, on the 5th, a steelmaking-related inter-provincial conference will be held within the Ministry of Commerce and Industry to discuss concrete plans. However, this is the first stage of establishing a national policy of steelmaking for national defense purposes, so its main focus is on production, establishing self-sufficiency in pig iron and steel. In peacetime, it relies on imports from China, the South Seas, and India, and in times of emergency, measures will be taken to install weak mines domestically and mainly develop the Maosan mine in Korea, and discuss resource development strategies in South Manchuria Railway. (Domei News Agency, 4th)

Japan Establishes Korean-Manchurian Colonization Company Under the Jurisdiction of the Korean Governor-General 20

(Tokyo) The Korean Governor-General's Office has approved the establishment of the Korean-Manchurian Colonization Joint-Stock Company with a capital of 20 million yen. It will be approved by the Colonial Affairs Ministry on the 4th, and the order will be announced in the Korean Governor-General's Official Gazette. The establishment committee of the company will be appointed by the Korean Governor-General, with the Director-General of Political Affairs, Imatada, as the chairman, to prepare for the establishment of the company. The content of the Korean-Manchurian Colonization Joint-Stock Company Order is as follows:

Chapter 1: General Provisions (1) The Korean-Manchurian Colonization Company will engage in necessary colonization projects for the resettlement of people from northwestern Korea. It will also provide funds for colonization projects for Korean resettlers in "Manchukuo." (2) The company may increase its capital before all shares are paid. (3) Shares are registered. Japanese nationals and their corporations, as well as "Manchukuo" people and their corporations, may own them. (4) The duration of existence is set at 30 years but may be extended with the approval of the Korean Governor-General.

Chapter 2: Staff (1) The company will have one president, three or more directors, and two or more auditors. (2) The president will be appointed by the Korean Governor-General, with a term of five years. The directors will be elected from shareholders holding 50 or more shares, with twice the number of candidates as the required number of directors, and formally appointed by the Korean Governor-General, with a term of four years. The auditors will be elected from shareholders holding 30 or more shares, with a term of two years. (3) The president and directors are not allowed to hold both positions unless approved by the Korean Governor-General.

Chapter 3: Business (omitted)

Chapter 4: Bonds (1) The Korean-Manchurian Colonization Company may issue Korean-Manchurian Colonization Bonds. (2) The Korean-Manchurian Colonization Bonds will have a face value of 10 yuan or more and will be unregistered with interest coupons. However, upon request of the applicant or owner, they may be changed to registered bonds. (2) When issuing Korean-Manchurian Colonization Bonds with a face value of 20 yuan or less, the sales period may be limited. (4) The statute of limitations for Korean-Manchurian Colonization Bonds is 25 years for the principal and five years for the interest. (5) Regulations for issuing exchange bonds and canceling purchased bonds.

Chapter 5: Supervision (1) The Korean Governor-General supervises the company and may issue necessary orders for supervision. (2) If the Korean Governor-General considers that the company's resolutions or the staff's actions violate laws or the company's articles of association or harm public interests, he may cancel the resolutions or dismiss the staff.

Chapter 6: Penal Regulations (omitted) (4th Associated Press)

Kong Orders All Provinces to Assist in Anti-Smuggling, Ministry of Finance Stipulates Types of Goods to Be Inspected, Ansier Consults in Tianjin Yesterday on Anti-Smuggling Situation 21

(Nanjing) Finance Minister Kong telegraphed to the authorities of all provinces and cities on the 4th, requesting assistance in anti-smuggling. The original telegram stated, "The government has previously promulgated measures to prevent smuggling by land transport, as well as implementing detailed rules, provisional regulations for punishing tax evasion, temporary regulations for inspecting the transportation and sale of imported goods, and the Ministry has stipulated generous reward measures and established tip-off boxes. These have all been reported successively and are now being earnestly implemented according to the aforementioned regulations. However, this matter is of great importance. The loss to the national treasury is significant, and legitimate merchants suffer greatly, affecting the market and causing pain. Currently, smuggled goods may flood the inland areas, relying on the full assistance of local military and police. I hereby telegraph to request you to instruct your subordinates to comply with and implement this, and I will be most grateful." (4th Central News Agency)

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Finance has added seven items to the reward measures for tip-offs, stipulating that tip-off boxes should be set up in customs and branch customs locations, allowing general merchants and civilians to submit documents to report smuggling, sale of smuggled goods, and concealment of smuggled goods. A circular telegram has been sent to all provincial and municipal governments to announce this to the public. (4th Central News Agency)

(Nanjing) Based on the provisions of the Temporary Regulations for Inspecting the Transportation and Sale of Imported Goods, the Ministry of Finance has appropriately stipulated the types of goods to be inspected, the various ash slurry buckets, the styles of the two types of licenses for transportation and sale, and the registration and licensing methods for merchants, factories, and transshipment companies. These were circulated to various locations on the 4th, instructing them to comply. The regulations are as follows: (A) According to Article 1, Section 2 of the regulations, the types of goods to be inspected are rayon, alcohol, alcoholic beverages, whiskey, brandy, champagne, gin, Japanese sake, various sweet wines, aniline dyes, rubber boots, rubber shoes, rubber tires, canned food, cigarette paper, cosmetics and perfumes, electrical materials, dry batteries, needles, kerosene, diesel, various piece goods, dried scallops, and various dried seafood. (B) According to Article 9 of the regulations, the styles of transportation licenses and sales licenses (styles omitted). Transportation licenses are printed and prepared by the customs, and sales licenses are printed and prepared by trade associations or joint factory associations, and a handling fee may be charged, not exceeding 5 fen in national currency per license. (C) According to Article 10 of the regulations, the registration and licensing methods for merchants, factories, and transshipment companies that wholesale, purchase, and transship various imported goods that should be inspected: (1) These methods are formulated in accordance with Article 10 of the Temporary Regulations for Inspecting the Transportation and Sale of Imported Goods. (2) All wholesalers, purchasers, or transshipment companies, etc., shall prepare a license application form within 20 days from the date of promulgation of these methods in the local area and register with the agency designated by the Ministry of Finance to obtain a license. (3) When merchants and transshipment companies prepare a license application form, they shall also obtain a certificate from the local trade association. If there is no local trade association, they shall obtain a certificate from the local chamber of commerce. When factories prepare a license application form, they shall obtain a certificate from the local joint factory association. If there is no local joint factory association, they shall obtain a certificate from the local chamber of commerce. (4) The licenses are prepared, numbered, and stamped by the Ministry of Finance. In addition to being issued by the customs, they are also issued to the provincial finance departments for distribution to the counties. Wholesalers, factories, and transshipment companies in trading ports shall apply to the customs. Other locations shall apply to the counties or entrust legal entities to apply on their behalf (in Peiping, applications shall be made to the office of the customs resident in Peiping managing the branch customs posts along the Great Wall). (5) Each license costs one yuan in national currency for labor and materials, and a new license shall be exchanged every twelve months. (6) The application forms for merchants to apply for licenses and the certificates issued by legal entities shall be prepared and filled out in accordance with the prescribed format. (7) When exchanging licenses, the old license number, date, and type shall be indicated and the new license shall be exchanged through the legal entity that originally issued the certificate. (8) If a merchant, factory, or transshipment company needs to add or change the number, a new license shall be obtained. (9) When applicants receive a new license, they shall surrender the old license at the same time, and the same shall apply when they cease operations. (3rd Central News Agency)

(Tianjin) Li Tonghua, Deputy Director of the Anti-Smuggling Inspectorate of the Ministry of Finance, arrived in Tianjin from Jinan on the morning of the 4th. In the afternoon, he visited Customs Commissioner Hillier and consulted with Anti-Smuggling Customs Commissioner Sprague. In the afternoon, he inspected the smuggling situation at the Beining East Station with Ansier and others. At 3 p.m., they discussed the establishment of an inspection office to prevent smuggling at the Customs public affairs room. Hillier provided recent relevant reports for reference. They adjourned at 6 p.m., and Li Tonghua returned south by night train. Ansier also plans to return to Beijing on the evening of the 5th to report. The establishment of the Tianjin Inspection Office is important and requires review and decision by the Ministry of Finance. (4th Special Dispatch)

(Tianjin) Ansier, Director of the Anti-Smuggling Inspectorate of the Ministry of Finance, will return south after consulting with Chen Juesheng in Tianjin. Deputy Director Li Tonghua came to Tianjin on the morning of the 4th to report to Ansier and left for Jinan by night train. (4th Central News Agency)

(Tianjin) The Tianjin Customs held a meeting on the afternoon of the 4th. Ansier, Li Tonghua, Hillier, Shapiro, and many senior customs officials attended. During the meeting, they meticulously discussed the prevention of smuggling by land transport and the organization of inspection sub-offices, based on the methods promulgated by the Ministry of Finance and in light of the local situation, and made a final decision. The customs also submitted various reports for reference. (4th Central News Agency)

(Tianjin) Li Tonghua said, "I was ordered to come north to prepare for the establishment of inspection offices in various places. Sub-offices have been established in Bengbu, Xuzhou, Jinan, and other places, so many smuggled goods have been seized in these areas recently. My visit to Tianjin is investigatory in nature. Smuggling is rampant in North China, and the central government has firmly established preventive measures, urging subordinates to earnestly implement them. Because there are important matters to report to the ministry, I will return south on the night of the 4th." (4th Special Dispatch)

(Tianjin) Li Tonghua, Deputy Director of the Anti-Smuggling Inspectorate of the Ministry of Finance, said, "I was ordered to go north to organize inspection sub-offices in various places. Sub-offices have been established in Bengbu, Xuzhou, Jinan, and other places, and many smuggled goods have been seized recently. This visit to Tianjin is of an inspection nature. Smuggling is rampant in North China, and I will resolutely comply with the measures set by the central government and earnestly investigate and suppress it. I will leave Tianjin for Jinan and return to Beijing on the evening of the 4th due to business. Ansier is also scheduled to return to Beijing on the 5th." (5th Central News Agency)

(Jinan) 290 tons of smuggled sugar were seized at the Jinpu Station. Fifty or sixty Koreans forcibly took it away, injuring Ye Yuchun, the anti-smuggling director, and Zhao Binglin, the police section chief. (4th Special Dispatch)

(Xuzhou) The Xuzhou Garrison Station recently received an order to start preventing smuggling due to the recent rampant smuggling activities. In addition to strictly ordering all railway police to earnestly assist the station masters in anti-smuggling, the station masters should implement any requests for assistance immediately without delay. All garrison troops along the Jinpu, Longhai, and Jiaoji railways have also been ordered to handle this. (4th Central News Agency)

Ma Yinchu Speaks on Methods to Prevent Smuggling 22

(Nanjing) Ma Yinchu spoke on the best methods to prevent smuggling at the Central Broadcasting Station on the 3rd. He first said that after the European War, we gained two major points: one was that justice triumphs over might, and the other was that those with insufficient resources cannot achieve final victory. After Italy annexed Abyssinia, these two major principles that were roughly established after the war were overturned. Examining Italy's methods of overturning, it was through controlled economy, tightly organizing groups on one hand and increasing production efficiency on the other. Therefore, it is known that even organized impoverished countries can achieve final victory. Secondly, he said that China's poverty is not true poverty, because there are many resources hidden underground that have not yet been developed. Italy, on the other hand, has very few natural resources, making it truly poor. Yet, it can achieve great results with a controlled economy. China can even implement a controlled economy, tightly organize, and develop rich resources, and its effectiveness will certainly be above Italy. Moreover, Italy controls for offense, while we control for defense. The difficulty is vastly different, which is obvious. It is only that the Chinese people should have self-confidence. China's method of controlled economy is different from that of foreign countries. Foreign countries emphasize external control, while China emphasizes internal control. The scope does not have to be very broad, and it can be done by starting with the following matters: (1) control of transportation, (2) control of currency, and (3) control of industrial and commercial groups. The first two items have made progress through the efforts of the government, but special attention should be paid to the third item. To control industrial and commercial groups, it is necessary to start with organization, making them strong and powerful, and strengthening the powers of existing guilds and chambers of commerce. Because the original Guild Law stipulated the adoption of a laissez-faire policy, it should now be changed to an interventionist policy. All industries must join the guild, and the guild must join the chamber of commerce. If this can be done, not only can the current smuggling problem be solved, but other problems can also be easily solved. Today's smuggling not only destroys the national tax system but also shakes the foundation of the national economy. If it continues to be rampant, it would be too laissez-faire and too free. Intervention and control can maintain the overall interests, so there is a need for intervention and control. Ma did not call the guild a horizontal organization, and the chamber of commerce is a vertical organization. It goes without saying that they have a close relationship. Moreover, industries should help each other and communicate with each other. For example, banks should not lend money to those who handle smuggled goods, transshipment companies should not transport smuggled goods, and porters should not unload smuggled goods. These are all examples. Since industries have helped each other, the public and private sectors should cooperate even more. Unscrupulous merchants will not be able to stand, and will not the smuggling problem be solved from then on? (4th Central News Agency)

Japan Resists Australian Wool 24

(Tokyo) Japan, based on the initiation of the Australian Trade Protection Act, restricts the amount of Australian wool purchased. It is reported that the Chairman of the Wool Industry Association, Kawanishi, recently visited relevant cabinet members, and as a result of the agreement, the opinions of government and civilians were unanimously decided as follows:

The amount of wool purchased from Australia is limited to one-third of the previous amount, that is, 250,000 bales.

Purchase 250,000 bales of wool from South America and New Zealand.

Because there is still a shortage of 250,000 bales, the wool industry is implementing a 30% reduction in work.

The government's decision does not clarify the quantity restriction, so the above quantities only represent its limits. However, it is noteworthy that wool industrialists have abandoned their previous attitude and are determined to implement major restrictions. (4th Associated Press)

Financial Panic and Serious Labor Unrest, New French Government Established, Political Undercurrents Lurk in Labor Unrest, Franc Falls, Gold Group Shaken, Socialist Premier in Dilemma 26

(Paris) The cabinet members of the Sarraut government went to the Presidential Palace today to submit their resignations, and the new government organized by Socialist leader Blum officially took office. (4th Reuters)

(Paris) Former Prime Minister and current Mayor of Lyon Herriot was elected Speaker of the House of Representatives today, receiving 377 votes. Another right-wing member of parliament received 150 votes. (4th Reuters)

(Paris) The franc suffered setbacks again today, its price falling to 76.48. After the British Equalization Fund provided significant assistance, it returned to 76.44. All parties are now asking each other, "Has the gold group reached the end of its rope?" The number of individuals selling small amounts increased sharply today, exceeding the number of large sales, indicating that public panic has gradually become widespread.

Those with informed sources in the foreign exchange market now feel that the new Premier Blum is facing an increasingly difficult situation due to the labor unrest. Political undercurrents lurk in the labor unrest, which is gradually becoming clear. The general opinion is that the new government will not want to attempt to lower the value of the currency in this turbulent atmosphere, so as not to fall into a political storm and be unable to extricate itself. It will probably implement some kind of exchange restriction as a temporary measure.

The French Treasury is now gradually reaching its borrowing limit, so it is probably unavoidable that it will directly rely on the Bank of France. If so, then it will be necessary to select someone with similar opinions to the "Popular Front" to replace the current president of the Bank of France. This kind of atmosphere is making the public's panic even more intense.

British industry is quite concerned that the current high exchange rate of the pound against various gold coins will weaken Britain's import trade position. The strength of the pound has caused the price of gold to continue to fall to 138 shillings and 3.5 pence. However, it is worth noting that when the price of the franc was 76.50 in 1934, the price of gold only reached 137 shillings and 2 pence, which reflects the current increase in demand for hoarding.

According to a report released by the Bank of England today, the number of British pound banknotes purchased by the European continent for hoarding is enormous. The number of British pound banknotes in circulation has increased by £7,000,000, reaching a total of £433,000,000, which is a new record. At the same time, according to a Reuters dispatch from Paris, the Bank of France released a report today stating that it lost gold worth 437,000,000 francs in the week ending May 29. Gold reserves have fallen from 62.37 to 61.01. (4th Reuters)

French Labor Unrest Escalates, Approaching Revolutionary Nature, Labor-Management Negotiations Have Broken Down, Armaments Factory Workers Also Strike 27

(Paris) Negotiations between metal industry employers and striking workers have broken down. They have now written to the new Premier Blum, saying that the situation is serious and unprecedented, approaching a revolutionary nature, and the government should be responsible for resolving it. The strike wave shows no signs of weakening. Three thousand munitions workers in Valenciennes, who are currently manufacturing heavy artillery shells and cannons, also joined the strike today. Thousands of miners in Anzin also stopped work, occupying the mine shafts and demanding wage increases. There are now fears that the strike will extend to the press, as the strikers at the Hachette building, which distributes newspapers, have set up pickets, and the lack of paper for printing newspapers has been greatly reduced due to the strike of transport carters. There is also a risk of strikes on public buses and underground trains. Many gasoline sales outlets have already closed. Bakers are also demanding wage increases and are likely to strike as well. It is now expected that the new Premier Blum will promulgate laws to curb the labor unrest and implement a 40-hour work week. Blum hopes to formulate the administrative outline of the "Popular Front" within two months, and the various departments will implement its details. The strike of transport carters has made it impossible to distribute the "L'Intransigeant" after it is printed. It is estimated that other newspapers will also be affected by the strike soon. (4th Reuters)

(Paris) The strike wave is expanding further today. Newspapers are unable to be distributed because the distributors are all on strike. Cars on the streets have also been greatly reduced due to the strike of gasoline distributors. The number of strikers has now reached 400,000, accounting for more than 360 factories. (4th National Gazette)

(Paris) The French strike wave has a tendency to spread across the country and there are fears that a general strike will occur nationwide on the occasion of the establishment of the new left-wing cabinet. According to today's estimates, at least 250,000 workers in various industries are on strike. The American-owned Hotchkiss factory has 11,000 strikers. Most of the gas plants in Paris have been closed. Civil servants are also planning to join the strike tomorrow. Although there are many rumors, the People's Front issued a statement today acknowledging the loss of the general strike reported by foreigners. (3rd National Gazette)

(Paris) The strike movement of staying in the factory without working has now spread to the steel mills of Terne and Anzin. 3,700 workers threatened that if the employers could not satisfy them, they would shut down the furnaces. Agricultural workers in the area near Paris are also now on strike. Workers in the gas, electricity, railway, and public transportation industries have all threatened to join the strike today. According to trade union claims, 230 factories in one area of Paris have been shut down, greatly affecting food and other supplies. (3rd Reuters)

(Paris) The ice factory strikers have resumed work because the employers have accepted their demands, so the main panic about the city's food supply has been removed. But as one wave subsides, another rises. The employees of major oil companies have also gone on strike, staying in the company and not working. If a solution is not found quickly, oil reserves will be exhausted within a few days, and public and private transportation may be disrupted. The new government took office today. Interior Minister Salengro issued a warning, saying that the new government cannot tolerate illegal activities by workers, and those occupying factories should leave quickly. The total number of strikers is still estimated to be over 250,000. (4th Reuters)

(Paris) The strike wave has now expanded and is sufficient to produce various economic consequences, so the current situation is quite serious. In total, there are as many as 100,000 strikers in the capital area, and 250,000 in various parts of the country. Those who joined the strike in the capital today include Hachette Newspaper Distribution Company, Coty Perfume Factory, Pathé-Nathan United Film Company, etc. Among them, Hachette Company is the only company in the country that operates the newspaper distribution business. It is estimated that a compromise between labor and management can be reached tonight to end the labor unrest. The bakery workers are scheduled to meet tonight, and the chemical industry union is scheduled to meet tomorrow morning in order to decide the attitude of each industry towards the labor unrest. At the same time, water tower workers have also joined the strike. Newspaper stacks are occupied by workers, and ink factories have stopped working, so there is a risk that there will be no water to drink and no newspapers to read in Paris. In the government and trade union sectors, every effort should be made to preserve various public utilities, especially water, gas, and electricity, so that they can continue to work as usual. As for the provinces, textile workers in the northern provinces and dock workers in Marseilles, workers in automobile factories in Toulouse have all joined the strike. The demands are the same as those in the capital area, namely, increasing wages and allowing trade unions to represent workers in signing labor contracts with employers. So far, fortunately, there have been no disturbances in any part of the country. The current cabinet and future cabinet ministers, as well as trade union leaders, are paying close attention to the strike situation. In particular, the trade unions are eager to control the strike and prevent it from going off the rails. The future Minister of Interior and current Mayor of Lille Salengro recently gave a speech at a meeting of deputies from the left-wing People's Front, saying that the current strike situation is intolerable to the authorities, and it is hoped that the Communist Party and various trade unions will cooperate in mediation so that the strike can be ended quickly. He also said, "Whether trade union leaders can control the masses is an important issue that we should understand. Our responsibility is to guide the workers and control the labor movement, so that after the People's Front wins the election, anarchy does not arise. The victory of the People's Front is to guarantee peace and maintain order in the future cabinet. After the future cabinet comes to power, it should submit a bill to the House of Representatives, so that the working class can be patient for a moment and wait and see." After Salengro finished speaking, a Communist Party member replied that national order had not been disturbed, and that in order to resolve the strike, the 40-hour work week system should be implemented immediately. The trade union leaders also met in the evening of the same day to discuss what measures should be taken to control the labor movement. The current Prime Minister Sarraut and Interior Minister Frossard recently declared to the press that the representatives of labor and management are expected to reach an agreement tomorrow, so that the trade unions can quickly sign labor contracts with employers. (3rd Havas)

(Paris) The total number of strikers in the suburbs has now increased to more than 350,000. The strike wave is spreading rapidly, like a prairie fire, causing anxiety to the current government and the orthodox socialists who are about to take power. Even the trade unions are feeling at a loss. From this, it can be seen that this strike was not initiated by the trade unions. It was actually caused by the workers themselves, who have been suffering for a long time, taking the opportunity to launch it on their own. The United General Confederation of Labor and the Paris Federation of Trade Unions recently jointly issued a declaration, requesting that the striking workers should continue to supply milk and other major foods to the elderly, young, and sick as usual. In addition, according to reports from various sources, although this strike wave has lasted for a week, the striking workers have been able to strictly maintain discipline, and it is unlikely to degenerate into a general strike, and there is no other political effect. This is because trade union leaders have repeatedly stated that once the employers accept the workers' demands, the workers will resume work. (4th Havas)

(Paris) The metallurgical factory owners recently notified Prime Minister Sarraut and Labor Minister Frossard that if the striking workers do not leave the factories immediately, it will be inconvenient to negotiate with their representatives. As for local security, they should ask the government to maintain it. (4th Havas)

Palestine - State of Terror Throughout the Territory - Two Bridges Blown Up 29

Jerusalem - Although Palestine currently has five battalions of British troops stationed there, and the authorities have promulgated new emergency regulations, the state of terror throughout the territory has not subsided in the slightest. Two bridges on the Hebron road were blown up this morning at dawn. Due to the damage to the road, only very light vehicles can now pass through. In addition, approximately one mile of telephone lines was also destroyed. Last night, while British patrol police were patrolling the narrow streets of the old city, they were shot at, but fortunately no one was hit. (Reuters dispatch, 4th)

Haifa - A Jewish-owned bus was bombed today, injuring six Jews, one Egyptian, and one Arab, all of whom were sent to the hospital. Two people were arrested at the scene. (Reuters dispatch, 4th)

Jerusalem - The situation in Palestine remains serious. The situation in Jaffa is relatively calm, but still tense. An Arab man who murdered a Jewish woman has been sentenced by the court to fifteen years of imprisonment. However, Arab nationalist conspirators and agitators have not ceased their activities. Fortunately, their power is not enough to command the masses. For example, the Arab workers at a British-owned cigarette factory are still working as usual, and Arab customers are still seen in Jewish-owned banks and department stores. As for the Tel Aviv city market, since its opening, due to the tense situation and unsafe transportation, the number of visitors has not been as large as in previous years. It is now scheduled to open on the 6th of this month. (Havas dispatch, 4th)

(Berlin) The foreign affairs director of the National Socialist Party, Rosenberg (i.e., the advocate of neo-paganism), recently published an article in the party's official newspaper, the "People's Observer," commenting on the situation in British Mandate Palestine. He stated: "In Palestine, the rights of the Arab people have been trampled upon. If Britain can adopt a policy of appeasement towards this people, the impact will extend to the entire Muslim world, which can be kept obedient and free from trouble. This policy not only conforms to the former British Foreign Secretary Lord Balfour's declaration (Note: Balfour issued a declaration on November 2, 1917, guaranteeing the Zionist movement's activities in Palestine, but also stated that the sovereignty of non-Jewish peoples should not be harmed), but also allows the Jews in Palestine to migrate to border areas and let them live in their original settlements, so as not to cause conflict with the Arab people." (Havas dispatch, 4th)

Reuters Commodity Report, June 4th 33

Gold and Silver: London gold prices were weak today, down six and a half pence from yesterday to 138 shillings and three and a half pence.

London bullion: The silver market was stable today, with spot and futures prices remaining at 19 pence 9375, the same as yesterday. India was reported to have bought, and China sold.

Mountree Silver Market: This morning was stable. The July futures price opened at 45.10-45.45, up eight pounds from yesterday's close.

Exchange Rates:

Anglo-American: The London foreign exchange market was slightly mixed this morning. The price of the pound sterling in terms of US dollars was still firm. The Anglo-American exchange rate opened at $5.02875, up eight hundred and seventy-five from yesterday's US-British close. It continued to rise by six hundred and twenty-five a few minutes later, fell back by one hundred and eighty-seven and a half at eleven o'clock, and rose again by one hundred and twenty-five at one o'clock in the afternoon, to $5.034375.

Securities: New York - The securities market opened with speculative pressure and fell slightly. The market situation then turned mixed, with price fluctuations limited to fractions and a downward trend. Merchants adopted a wait-and-see attitude, awaiting developments in the Washington tax bill. The economic and political situation in France had an adverse impact on the market. At noon, the prices of most major securities fell by one-quarter to one pound. The New York stock market prices are listed on the left.

Cotton and Wheat:

Liverpool Wheat Market: The opening this morning was calm, due to the strength of the pound sterling, which made French wheat prices slightly cheaper, and the private estimates last night were also favorable to the short sellers. A batch of Australian wheat that failed to sell has now been shipped to the Liverpool market for sale, causing market prices to fall. At one o'clock in the afternoon, the July futures price fell by 25 to 5 shillings, 7 pence, and 875.

Liverpool Cotton Market: American cotton futures were down today. At one o'clock in the afternoon, the July futures price was 6.17, down three pounds.

New York Cotton Market: The weather news this morning was favorable to the short side, so the bulls rose to liquidate, causing the market to loosen slightly. At noon, the October futures price was 10.74, down four pounds from yesterday's close.

Chicago Wheat Market: This morning was stable, due to speculation buying caused by reports of continued dry weather in the Northwest. At noon, the September futures price rose by 75 to 85.375. Coarse grains rose slightly with the wheat market.

Rubber: London - Today was stable. At one o'clock in the afternoon, the transaction prices for the July and September futures were unchanged, remaining at 7 pence 3125.

New York - Reports that the International Rubber Restriction Committee had stipulated an increased third-quarter quota, and the current situation in France, were all unfavorable to the New York rubber market. Famous American Nurse Passes Away 35

(Washington) Miss Noyes, the most famous figure in the history of American nursing, has passed away here. Miss Noyes graduated from the nursing department of Johns Hopkins Hospital in 1896 and soon became a prominent figure in the profession. She held various important positions in the American Nurses Association and served as the first vice president of the International Council of Nurses. In 1923, she received the International Red Cross Nightingale Medal for her great contributions to the nation and wounded soldiers, and was awarded an honorary medal by the French government. She wrote many nursing books and articles. (Reuters dispatch, 3rd)

Speaker of the US House of Representatives Passes Away 36

(Washington) Speaker of the House of Representatives Byrns died suddenly of a heart attack here today at the age of sixty-seven. Byrns was elected in September 1924 to succeed the late Lenroot as Speaker. Last autumn, he and his wife accompanied a delegation of congressmen to the Far East to attend the inauguration of the Philippine Commonwealth government on November 16. He visited Shanghai en route. (National Telegraph, 3rd)

(Washington) The House of Representatives Speaker Byrns passed away yesterday from a vascular occlusion, and today the House adjourned for one day to mourn. The government has scheduled a state funeral for Byrns this Saturday. President Roosevelt will personally attend the funeral. Byrns previously traveled to Manila to attend the inauguration of the Philippine independent government in February of last year, along with the country's Vice President, Ghana, and made a brief stopover in Shanghai. (Havas dispatch, 4th)

Albanian King Arrives in London - Tens of Thousands Welcome Him - Issues Written Statement to Journalists - Says Resistance Lasted Seven Months and Failed Due to Poison Gas - Decides to Go Abroad to Appeal to the World for Justice 37

(London) The King of Abyssinia held a meeting with journalists in the main living room of the country's embassy this morning, but did not speak. Instead, the embassy secretary read a written statement, which stated in part: "My country never had any intention of war. It was only when a strong enemy invaded our territory that we rose up to resist. Our people's armaments were inferior and unprepared, but they still resisted for seven months. In the end, we failed because the enemy army used poison gas, causing our soldiers and civilians to suffer terrible poisoning and burns, which we could not defend against. After much deliberation, I could only see two paths: one was to allow the enemy army to annihilate our entire nation, and the other was to go abroad myself and appeal to all countries, asking them to uphold justice. The League of Nations Covenant is the product of the painful sacrifices of the World War. If we allow it to be destroyed and remain silent, it is tantamount to allowing all of humanity to submit to might." After the secretary finished reading, the Albanian King bowed to the journalists and withdrew. (Havas dispatch, 4th)

(London) The Albanian King arrived at Waterloo Station today with his two sons, two daughters, and General Gaza. There was a large welcome, with rows of people shoulder to shoulder, some twenty deep. They took off their hats and cheered. Foreign Secretary Eden sent a private secretary to officially welcome him, which is the customary practice when a foreign monarch is traveling incognito in England. Among the dignitaries gathered at the station were the treasurer and chairman of the former Independent Labour Party, Lord Airlie, the economic reporter Sir Layton, the famous writer and speaker Sir Angell, and many Albanian expatriates, all of whom were wearing Albanian-style garments over European clothing. The Albanian King's two sons were dressed in dark blue clothes with floral designs, and his two daughters were wearing the most fashionable European clothes. General Gaza was wearing white Albanian clothes. The waiting crowd waved Albanian flags, which were distributed by an English woman, and read out several welcoming speeches. One was issued by the Indian representative to London. After the speeches, the King and his entourage entered cars, and the cheers resumed. The Albanian King raised his hat in thanks. A police escort led the way in front of the cars, heading straight to the magnificent residence of the wealthy merchant and philanthropist Sir Khadouri, who is currently in Shanghai. He telegraphed the Albanian King, offering his house as a place for the King to stay in London, which the Albanian King accepted. (Reuters dispatch, 3rd)

(London) When the King of Abyssinia arrived here today, he was welcomed by tens of thousands of people. The situation was extremely enthusiastic. British public opinion clearly shows sympathy for Abyssinia. Political figures therefore predict that relations between Britain and Italy will become strained again. It is said that if the Albanian King resolutely decides to attend the League of Nations meeting in Geneva in person, Italy may withdraw from the alliance, and Britain can still negotiate with Italy separately outside the scope of the League of Nations. However, the British government will eventually advise the Albanian King not to make this trip. Foreign Secretary Eden met with the Italian Ambassador Grandi today. The conversation was not affected by the Albanian King's arrival. However, the discussion was still broad and vague, and there was no progress in the rapprochement between Britain and Italy. This is because Italy is unwilling to show a spirit of compromise to the League of Nations, and this determination remains unchanged. Britain, on the other hand, believes that the Italo-Ethiopian issue should first be resolved within the framework of the League of Nations, and only then can a way be found to adjust relations between Britain and Italy. Generally speaking, the British government is still willing to approach Italy. Experts at the Foreign Office are now seeking a solution that would achieve a win-win situation between Italy and the League of Nations, that is, to enable Italy to rejoin the collective security system while the League of Nations is not forced to recognize Italy's established fact of annexing Abyssinia. Once this plan is formulated, a compromise between Britain and Italy may be possible. (Havas dispatch, 3rd)

League of Nations General Assembly - Decides to Convene Early - Scheduled for the 20th of This Month 38

(London) In order to respond to Argentina's request to convene an extraordinary session of the General Assembly urgently to consider the issue of sanctions against Italy, the League of Nations plans to advance the date of the General Assembly in September and convene it within four weeks, probably on June 29. The League of Nations Executive Council was originally scheduled to meet on June 16 to discuss the sanctions issue, but due to this development, it has now been postponed to the end of June. In addition, the meeting of the signatory countries of the Dardanelles Strait Convention, which was originally scheduled to be convened in Montreux in the near future, has also been postponed to July. Argentina and other Latin American countries are now making every effort to oppose the lifting of sanctions against Italy. (Reuters dispatch, 4th)

(London) Regarding Argentina's request to convene the League of Nations General Assembly in advance, Foreign Secretary Eden has exchanged phone calls with Czech President Benes (the chairman of the current League of Nations General Assembly) and League of Nations Secretary-General Drummond. It has been decided that the meeting will be convened on the 20th of this month. As for the extraordinary meeting of the Executive Council, which was originally scheduled to be convened on the 16th of this month, it may be postponed to the 26th of this month. (Havas dispatch, 4th)

(Geneva) The convening of the League of Nations General Assembly on the 20th of this month has been confirmed by League of Nations officials. The extraordinary meeting of the Executive Council will be convened on the 25th or 26th of this month. (Havas dispatch, 4th)

(London) Well-informed sources have declared that the League of Nations General Assembly will be convened on the 20th of this month. The chairman was originally Czech Foreign Minister Benes, but he has now been elected as President of the country and will therefore not be able to continue to serve as chairman. At that time, British Foreign Secretary Eden (the chairman of the current Executive Council) will serve as interim chairman until a new chairman is elected. (Havas dispatch, 4th)

Capital of Argentina - Regarding Argentina's request to convene the League of Nations General Assembly in advance, well-informed sources here have declared that Argentina's request was not instigated by any foreign country, but was entirely voluntary and supported by domestic public opinion. (Havas dispatch, 3rd)

(Rome) The Argentine Ambassador visited Undersecretary of Foreign Affairs Suvich today to explain the Argentine government's proposal to the League of Nations. Suvich stated that Italy is currently opposed to Argentina's proposal to convene an extraordinary session of the League of Nations General Assembly to consider the issue of sanctions against Italy, and said that the responsibility of the League of Nations General Assembly is to formulate general principles, and what is needed now is to formulate practical proposals to seek compromise. In addition to requesting the General Assembly to consider the issue of sanctions, Argentina also requested that the situation caused by the annexation of Abyssinia and the reform of the League of Nations should be considered. Yesterday, the Argentine government sent a telegram to the League of Nations, proposing that the League of Nations General Assembly should convene a meeting around June 16. (Reuters dispatch, 3rd)

(London) According to well-informed sources, the British government is quite favorable to Argentina's proposal to convene the League of Nations General Assembly in advance, but believes that it would be too early for the General Assembly to convene as early as the 15th of this month. Before the General Assembly convenes, diplomatic talks should first be held between the countries concerned to prepare, and the meeting of the Executive Council should make arrangements in advance so that the agenda can be completely arranged, and the representatives of the countries can bring clear instructions with them when they attend the General Assembly, without having to ask their governments for instructions at every turn. It is reported that the British government advocates that the General Assembly should convene on the 29th of this month. When Foreign Secretary Eden met with French Ambassador Corbin and South African High Commissioner de Villiers this afternoon, the date issue was discussed. (Havas dispatch, 3rd)

(London) The Times recently published a letter from its former editor, Stead, stating that if the current sanctions are lifted, it will entail great danger and must be treated with caution. He also said, "As far as the British Empire is concerned, if it is willing to accept the humiliation of defeat, there may be a risk of disintegration within the empire. To avoid this, before changing the strategy adopted by the League of Nations (referring to sanctions), some decisions must be made in advance. What are the decisions? First, all countries should refuse to recognize Italy's annexation of Abyssinia. Second, Italy needs money to develop Abyssinia, and all member states of the League of Nations should refuse to provide loans. Third, in the future, if there is any further act of aggression, all financial, economic, and military resources should be used to deal with the aggressor. There are many different opinions on whether to maintain or abolish sanctions, and the arguments are different. However, in any case, a fair assessment of this argument can only be made after the above three conditions have been met. Otherwise, abandoning sanctions is tantamount to abandoning the policy of collective security, which must be treated with caution." (Havas dispatch, 4th)

(Washington) State Department officials stated today that although the Italo-Ethiopian War has ended, President Roosevelt had previously warned the American people not to travel on Italian or Ethiopian ships. This warning remains in effect until it is canceled, and there is currently no consideration of canceling it. (National Telegraph, 3rd)

Educational Broadcasting Special

English Language Lectures: On Learning English for Middle School Students (Part 2) - Full-Time Editor, National Bureau of Compilation and Translation 41

— Zhou Qixun

Finally, there is sentence pattern imitation. Once ear training has yielded substantial results and oral imitation has a solid foundation, teachers can have students read English and imitate sentence construction. Junior and senior high school students have a great capacity for imitating sentences and should be encouraged to do so as much as possible. For example, if students already understand "I am Mr. Wong here yesterday," the teacher can have them replace "I" with words like "you," "we," and "they." Similarly, "saw" can be replaced with words like "met," "noticed," or "spoke to." Another example is transforming "I write the letter" into forms like "I write letters," "The letter is written," "I have the letter written," or "He has two letters written." This type of imitation enables students to actively use grammar, extrapolate, and practice repeatedly, which is extremely beneficial. Teachers should use this method frequently. This is the third method. If English is taught or learned using the above three methods, there is no reason for it not to be successful.

English Pronunciation

Among the three languages—English, German, and French—English pronunciation is the most difficult. Each English letter represents a wide variety of sounds within a word. If each letter consistently represented the same sound, pronunciation would be much easier, as is the case with German. The difficulty of English pronunciation lies here. Let's illustrate with some examples:

First—same letter, different sounds, for example:

Cat get exact man bin woman show

City gem estra human bind women cow

(and so on)

Second—same sound, different letters, for example:

Cat sit such bed win lies shows head light

Kitten City hutch said women buys go

(and so on)

Third—letter present but no sound, for example:

Knot graw fatique sign bough couldguard buy write awry right han Fkerchief psalm Programme and so on.

Fourth—different spelling but identical pronunciation, for example:

gnaw flower mourn caulk nose mode sewdd thyme hosrse nor; flour; morn; cork; knows; mowed; sowed; time; horse and so on.

From the examples above, we can see that English pronunciation is very irregular. We cannot pronounce a word based solely on its spelling. To compensate for this deficiency, the International Phonetic Alphabet is now widely used. The International Phonetic Alphabet is a system of phonetic symbols established by the International Phonetic Association. Currently, there are forty-six symbols. Each symbol represents a particular sound in English. Whenever that sound appears in an English word, it is represented by that symbol. The pronunciation of each symbol is constant. Therefore, by learning these symbols, we know how to pronounce words. There are two words in English whose pronunciation we often overlook: "of" and "off." These two words have different pronunciations: "of" is pronounced "ov," and "off" is pronounced "of." So, in the ordinary spelling of "of" and "off," we cannot see the difference in pronunciation, but if we consult An English Pronouncing Dictionarysc edited by Daniel Jneo, we will know how to pronounce them. Now, isn't it common for our newspapers to translate the British place names Birmingham, Buckingham, Cunningham, etc. as "Bo Ming Han"? This is incorrect. The reason for the mistranslation is that the translators saw "ham" at the end of the spelling of Birmingham, so they translated "ham" as "Han." Little did they know that the "h" in this word is silent. Therefore, it is clear that relying on spelling for pronunciation is not entirely reliable. Similarly, the English place names Worcester and Leicester are pronounced "wuso" and "lests," but if we are not careful or do not consult Daniel Jones's An English Pronouncing Dictionary, we will often make mistakes. Therefore, the International Phonetic Alphabet is very helpful for pronunciation. Furthermore, the word "the" is sometimes pronounced I (emphatir Jorm or before a vowel) and sometimes （before a consonant）. The letter "A" is sometimes pronounced "ei" (emphatic) and sometimes （unemphatic）. Students should pay attention to these distinctions. Currently, most English textbooks for senior high school students include International Phonetic Alphabet pronunciations for new words in each lesson, which is an improvement compared to the past, but they are still not fully utilized. The editors include them in the textbooks merely as a formality. So, when there are specific pronunciation issues that should be noted, they are not indicated with the International Phonetic Alphabet. We hope that teachers and students in junior and senior high schools will make greater use of the International Phonetic Alphabet. (End)

Large Quantity of Smuggled Sugar Confiscated in Jinan 84

The transporter forcibly demanded loading and unloading with an overbearing attitude. Li Tonghua argued on principle, resulting in a stalemate.

Jinan Dispatch: Recently, smuggled goods such as cigarettes, paper, and white sugar have been continuously arriving from Tianjin. Therefore, the central government specially established customs anti-smuggling offices along the Jinpu Railway at Xuzhou, Jinan, Dezhou, and other stations. On the 31st of last month, train No. 305 on the Pingpu line carried 50 tons of smuggled white sugar. On the 1st of this month, another 160 tons of smuggled white sugar were transported on train No. 305. All of these goods were transferred from the Beining Railway with connecting tickets. Li Tonghua, the deputy director of the Jinan Anti-Smuggling Inspection Office, ordered that all of them be detained in the rail yard, and the original train remained unmoved. At about 9:00 AM on the 2nd, about 50 people, some of whom were foreigners, arrived at the station. They first asked Li Tonghua for the white sugar that had been transported. Li, due to his duty, could not allow them to take it away. However, the other party insisted on loading and unloading. Seeing their unreasonable demands, Li immediately notified the consular office in Jinan by telephone. The consular office sent two people to the station. Li stated that he was ordered to inspect smuggled goods in Jinan. How could he allow them to evade customs duties? If they insisted on taking the goods away, the transporter had to submit the Tianjin Customs delivery documents before they could be released. However, the consular office representatives claimed that the goods could be transported away first, and then the procedures could be completed later. Furthermore, since the goods were transferred from the Beining Railway, why didn't Tianjin Customs inspect them and only detain them in Jinan? Li replied that it was precisely because the goods hadn't gone through customs procedures in Tianjin that they were being inspected and detained in Jinan. By 12:00 PM, there was still no resolution. At this time, Li Tonghua sent an urgent telegram to Tianjin Customs, requesting instructions on how to handle the situation. He also declared to the transporters that after waiting three or four hours, Tianjin should reply. If they allowed the release, he would allow the loading and unloading. Seeing that they were getting nowhere, more than 50 people crowded into the first-class waiting room and turned to negotiate with Station Master Wang of Jinan Station. They collectively said, "The Chinese are unreasonable. Our goods are transported by the Jinpu Railway. We only need to pick them up at the Jinan Station of the Jinpu Railway. We don't recognize any customs personnel in Jinan because we don't know about them, and our consulate hasn't received any notice. This Mr. Li must be an imposter deliberately making things difficult." After saying this, they forcibly ordered Station Master Wang to retrieve the goods from the freight yard, saying, "We will transport them ourselves." Wang replied that since the customs personnel did not allow unloading, he could not bear this responsibility. The stalemate lasted for a long time. Around 1:00 PM, the transporters, seeing that there was still no result, said to Station Master Wang, "You have counted our goods." Wang said, "Of course." The transporters then asked to see the freight yard, but Wang initially refused. After obtaining Li Tonghua's consent, they went to the freight yard together. The transporters saw that the original train had not been moved. They asked why they weren't allowed to unload. Wang and others said that they were not allowed to leave, but unloading was allowed. The station staff then unloaded the white sugar. It was already 3:00 PM. The transporters still had no solution and dispersed. How this matter will be handled in the future depends on negotiations. (2nd)

Details of Li Shengda's Assassination 85

Senior officials from Yan's faction thoroughly investigate the truth.

Taiyuan Dispatch: Li Shengda, a member of the Central Executive Committee and commander of the 19th Army, was suddenly assassinated at around 4:00 AM on the 30th of this month while inspecting defenses in Lishi County. He was shot in the head, a vital point, and died on the spot. The assassin was also shot and killed on the spot by Li's guards. Li was a prominent general in Shanxi Province and highly trusted by Jiang. Therefore, the news of his death caused widespread shock and grief. The details of the assassination and its aftermath are recorded below:

Details of the Assassination: According to Li Mingding, the chief of staff of the army, Commander Li was ordered to depart on the 26th of this month to Lishi to supervise his troops in crossing the river to Shaanxi to suppress the remnants of bandits. After Commander Li arrived in Lishi, he stayed at the Xiangji Company's kerosene store. Commander Li's stationing in a commercial firm was originally a temporary measure, as he did not want to affect the business of the firm. Therefore, although he was stationed inside the firm, the gate was not heavily guarded so that the firm could operate freely. Commander Li had been extremely busy in recent days coordinating the departure of his troops and handling military affairs. On the morning of the 29th, he gave a speech to a departing unit. On the morning of the 30th, as dawn was breaking, Li got up to give another speech. Just as he was preparing to depart, a rioter suddenly broke in and opened fire on Li. Li's guards, hearing the sound, rushed in and realized that it was an assassination attempt. In haste, they drew their pistols and returned fire on the rioter. Since the bullets hit vital points, Commander Li died immediately, and the rioter also died on the spot. Military personnel rushed to the scene to investigate and handle the aftermath. The speaker (Chief Li himself) hurriedly returned to the province to report. As for the origin of the rioter and whether he had any background, there are no clues yet.

Li's Brief Biography: Li Shengda, courtesy name Shumin, is currently 45 years old. He is from Jincheng County, Shanxi Province. He graduated from Baoding Military Academy. He rose through the ranks of the Shanxi military from the lowest level to his current position. In 1923, he was credited for defending Fanshi City during the Yanbei campaign. Within a year, he was promoted from battalion commander to division commander. During the Northern Expedition, the Shanxi army expanded, and he was appointed army commander. After the recovery of Tianjin and Beijing, he also served as the commander of the Pingjin Railway. In 1930, the Shanxi army was reorganized, and he was reduced to division commander under Fu Zuoyi. In the winter of the previous year, he was telegraphed by Chairman Jiang to go to Jiangxi. The division was reorganized into the 19th Army, and Li remained the commander. In the summer of last year, he was ordered to return to Shanxi and was appointed deputy commander of the Shaanxi Bandit Suppression Force. Last winter, he attended the Fifth Plenary Session as a representative of the Shanxi military and was elected as a member of the Central Executive Committee. This time, due to his meritorious service in suppressing bandits in western Shanxi, Yan greatly expanded the army and ordered him to lead the troops to Shaanxi to pursue and suppress the bandits to complete the mission.

Family Situation: Li came from a farming family. Both of his parents have passed away. He had five brothers. His eldest brother has also passed away. Li was the second oldest. His fourth brother, Li Shenglian, is an inspector for the provincial government. His fifth brother is currently residing in the province. The son of his eldest brother, Wenbin, serves as a counselor for the Suiyuan headquarters and principal of the Jincheng Huzhe Middle School. Li left behind four sons and one daughter. The eldest son is already over twenty years old and is currently studying at the Nanjing Central Military Academy. The rest are studying in the province. His wife is at home, and his concubine is currently residing in the province.

Li's Life: Li was a veteran general in the National Army. After graduating from Baoding Military Academy, he served in Shanxi Province. He was generous and had great integrity. He was meticulous in his duties, so he was valued by his superiors and admired by his colleagues. He was promoted to his current position. He experienced many battles and achieved significant military achievements. Chairman Jiang and Vice Chairman Yan both treated him with special favor. In the previous year, when the central government requisitioned the Shanxi army, Vice Chairman Yan planned to send a unit to Jiangxi. Li readily accepted the order, as he was dedicated to serving the Party and the country and fighting for the group. He had a clear vision and showed a deep understanding of righteousness. After arriving in Jiangxi, he spared no effort in searching for and suppressing the remnants of bandits. He captured important bandit leader Huang Zhichao and many important members of the bandit group and brought them to justice, causing the disintegration of several thousand Red bandits. Therefore, the Red bandits hated him intensely. Li emphasized discipline and loved the people when leading troops. He was always sincere in his words and actions. Wherever he went, he committed no offenses. When he was stationed in Ji'an for eight months, the local people all loved and respected him. When he was ordered to return to Shanxi last year, the people of Ji'an even sent telegrams to the central government to request him to stay. He was so highly respected. This is why Chairman Jiang and Vice Chairman Yan valued him even more. At the Fifth Plenary Session, he was elected as a member of the Central Executive Committee. He was naturally honest and treated people with great respect. He had a strong sense of national identity. Therefore, he was always willing to take responsibility. He was a rare talent of the times. Now he was killed by bandits before completing his mission. It is a great loss to our Party, our country, and Shanxi Province. Therefore, everyone who heard the news felt deep sorrow.

Preparations for the Aftermath: After the news of Li's assassination reached the province, Chairman Yan specially ordered Feng Pengzhu, the adjutant of the Suiyuan headquarters, to represent him in Lishi to handle Li's funeral arrangements and strictly investigate the cause of the assassination. Feng left this morning at 4:00 AM with Wang Jingguo, the commander of the 70th Division, by car to Lishi. Feng and Wang will stay there for about three or two days and then return to Taiyuan. Yan also convened a meeting of senior military officials in Taiyuan at the Suiyuan headquarters last night at 6:00 PM to discuss Li's funeral arrangements. It is said that Commander Li's body was placed in a coffin yesterday afternoon. All the coffins and other items were purchased and sent to Lishi by Chairman Yan. After the coffin was placed, the military, political, and academic circles of Lishi went to pay their respects. The coffin has been transported from Lishi to Taiyuan. After the coffin arrives in Taiyuan, it will be transported to his private residence on Beimen Street. It has been decided to establish a funeral committee, led by Li's friends Yang Wenqing and others, to handle all matters. Funeral services such as chanting scriptures and public memorial services will be held on a scheduled date.

Miscellaneous Writings on the Rural Areas of Hubei 86

(Special Correspondent Cheng Jun)

(15) What I Saw and Heard in Gucheng

Going north from Laohekou is the passage to Shaanxi, known as the Lao-Bai Road, which starts from Kou, passes through Gucheng, Jun County, Yunyang, and ends in Baihe, Shaanxi. It has great significance in military, political, and commercial terms. However, I heard that the director of the road bureau and local officials who presided over the construction of the road in the past had unspeakable difficulties. The construction of the roadbed, road surface, bridges, and culverts was extremely sloppy. The road surface was uneven, and the car traveled as if in a cloud. Passengers often hit their heads and bled. Once it rained, traffic would be blocked for days or even months. The government and the people suffered losses together. The road construction workers were conscripted locally without paying a penny, but the construction funds allocated by the government still reached more than 500,000 yuan. It is a great sigh that the Chinese people are unwilling to take things seriously. Recently, Wang Qiang, the director of the provincial highway bureau, has been trying his best to rectify it, but the northern section has been washed away by the water, and it is unknown when it will be repaired. Moreover, the staff at the road stations have a kind of arrogance, often insulting passengers. The staff at Kou Station are particularly bad. Passengers say that they are "as stupid as deer and pigs, as fierce as jackals and wolves," which is somewhat similar. It is difficult to reverse the accumulation of problems, and the whip is out of reach. The reporter boarded the car from Kou, not knowing where it could drive to, and let it rest northward. After traveling sixty miles to Gucheng, the road was blocked again due to a wind and rain overnight, and I was detained for several days.

The city was the fief of Duke Gu in the Zhou Dynasty, and later it was Zhuyang. At the end of the Ming Dynasty, Zhang Xianzhong's rebellion started here. Now it belongs to the Fifth Administrative Inspectorate District of Xiangyang. The atmosphere is extremely closed. Once you enter its territory, spring couplets such as "There are no two masters in the sky, only one supreme in the world" and "The emperor's grace is as vast as spring, and the cultural rule is as bright as the sun" often catch the eye, making people laugh and cry. Later, I heard that the county not only has low public intelligence, but also the education sector is the same. Moreover, there are many factions. There is a central primary school in the county seat. The principal is an old and decaying person with bad habits. Many teachers are incompetent. The special party headquarters of the 82nd Division used to be stationed here and ran a teacher research class. When the party headquarters was transferred, it came to an abrupt end. The trained teachers were all squeezed out. The education funds reach 20,000 yuan per year, but only 14,000 yuan is used, and the rest is unknown.

Although the countryside has suffered from years of drought and floods, its vitality has not been completely lost. Agricultural products include cotton, beans, wheat, millet, rice, and corn. Mountain areas produce tung oil, wood oil, mushrooms, medicinal materials, and fire paper. Land is measured in acres, with five feet square as one bow, and 240 square bows as one acre. Some use the area worked by a farmer's hoe or a bull's plow in a day as the standard of measurement, which is not accurate. There are many landlords. The top money exceeds one-third of the original value of the land, so capital is concentrated in the hands of landlords. Now it is a spring famine and rice is expensive, with each stone rising to fifteen yuan. Rich households hoard and speculate, unwilling to sell. In the Lengjiaji and Xinjiaji areas, there have been incidents of starving people smearing their faces with ink and gathering to rob rice. When the army rushed to the scene, they had already dispersed.

Last year's flood drowned thousands of people, and the city walls were destroyed. At that time, a certain division headquarters and special party headquarters were stationed here and worked hard to rescue them, saving the lives of tens of thousands of people. Later, the government allocated 20,000 yuan to the county government to handle agricultural relief. Because the seeds were sold at inflated prices and the soybeans were watered, the disaster victims returned them one after another. The county magistrate was dismissed because of this. Now in the spring relief, another 5,000 yuan has been received to repair the city and purchase grain for distribution. The purchased grain is corn, and it has not been distributed yet due to difficulties. Each work is two dimes, and it is heard that some disaster workers have not received funding, for some reason.

People are prone to litigation, and some sue for generations over trivial matters. There are not a few smokers. There are three soil plaster shops in the county seat, paying 400 yuan in Ding and other taxes per shop. There are also many prostitutes, and sanitation is not taken seriously. When the reporter arrived in the county, it was the time when the order was given to drive away prostitutes and carry out a cleanliness campaign, all of which were presided over by the army and the government. The Zhu regiment stationed there has been effective in maintaining law and order and assisting the people in building and repairing city dikes and streets, which it advocates, and the people praise it very much. The county magistrate is also quite capable and has as many as five wives and concubines, but it is said that he has not neglected his duties. He said, "Revitalizing the countryside does not require much talk, it only needs to maintain law and order and reduce exploitation." It can be said to be pertinent. The hope of all the peasants in Hubei is nothing more than this, and it is not only true of Gucheng County.

The gentry power in the area is quite high, especially with the Financial Affairs Committee as the backbone. The finances are controlled by them. Whether local undertakings can be smoothly promoted depends on the will of the chairman of the Financial Affairs Committee. Those who come to lead this place must be connected, otherwise, their administration will be subject to many restraints. This kind of evil force needs to be eradicated urgently. (Sent from Gucheng on May 16)

Smuggled Sugar Seized Again in Bengbu 87

Forty-two bags of tax-evading sugar, transported to Shanghai for customs handling.

Bengbu Dispatch: Smuggling in North China is like a raging tide, becoming increasingly unstoppable. Bengbu, located at the throat of the Jinpu Railway, connecting the north and the south, has become a place where tax-evading goods openly arrive in a continuous stream. After arriving in Bengbu, they are then distributed to various counties in northern Anhui. Since the establishment of the Anti-Smuggling Inspection Office of the Customs for preventing road transport smuggling in Bengbu, customs officers have been diligently inspecting passenger and freight cars coming from the north on the Jinpu Railway at the station every day. If tax-evading smuggled goods (i.e., goods without tax receipts) are found, they are detained. After more than 4,000 bags of smuggled sugar were seized at the freight station, smugglers have become wary and often try to circumvent the inspection by secretly transporting goods. However, the Bengbu District Consolidated Tax Administration, while inspecting privately made cigarette paper, inadvertently seized 42 bags of smuggled sugar in Songjiatan, eight miles away from Bengbu. The people and goods were taken to the office for questioning. After that, the smuggled sugar was transferred to the customs' Bengbu Inspection Office, loaded into a car that night, and transported to Shanghai for customs handling. Today (1st), the Inspection Office received a tip that a large number of smuggled sugar was being transported by ship to Shouxian. It has already made a long-distance phone call to the Shouxian authorities to intercept it.

Gold Mines in Northern Manchuria 88

The Japanese are actively planning to exploit them. The location is in the upper reaches of the Heilongjiang River.

Qiqihar Dispatch: The North Manchuria Gold Mining Co., Ltd., established by the Japanese, previously centered on the four major creeks in the upper reaches of the Heilongjiang River. With the help of the puppet organization, they forcibly obtained extensive mining rights, planning to extract placer gold. Since last summer, they have transported gold dredges and other necessities. However, due to freezing, they temporarily suspended operations, waiting for the ice to thaw this spring to resume work. Therefore, the company recently recruited technicians and workers to manufacture gold dredges, and all preparations have been made early. They are now constructing gold dredges and will officially start work within three months.

Xu Ziqing, who relayed it, was also involved in the bribery. When County Magistrate Li heard about this, he was furious and ordered them to be taken into custody last night. Wuxi Sets Up Warehouses in Various Counties 92

The Administrative Inspectorate of the Second District instructed the county governments of Wuxi, Suzhou, Wujiang, Jiangyin, Kunshan, Taicang, Changshu, and Jin, because the accumulation of supplies in each county in the district is different, either the amount of grain accumulated is small, or the deposited funds have not been used to purchase grain. And most counties often only have county warehouses, and many have no district, township, or town warehouses. If there is an extraordinary disaster, the entire damage can easily occur. It is necessary to prepare warehouses, pay attention to separate storage to prevent against potential issues. As for the amount stored, efforts must be made to increase it to achieve the purpose of actual preparation. At the same time, efforts should be made to advocate for the expansion of voluntary warehouses and private reserves, so that those who are enthusiastic about public welfare can happily donate, and those who are usually good at saving can store more, so as to achieve both public and private progress.

Plans to Build a Large-Scale Shopping Mall 93

This city is located in the center of Beijing and Shanghai, with convenient transportation and a prosperous commercial market. Pulling Water Chestnuts Leads to Murder 94

Deng Afu, a resident of Zhang Lane No. 13 outside Guangmen in this city, was 52 years old. He used to make a living by pulling water chestnuts. On the 31st of last month, Afu was again playing a water chestnut-pulling game with Zhou Yaoting, the owner of the Zhou Shunxing Iron Factory near Huinong Bridge. Because of a dispute over winning and losing, an argument broke out, followed by a physical fight. At that time, Afu suffered a serious kick to his lower abdomen. Although he invited injury specialist Wei Yunrui and doctors from Puren Hospital to diagnose and treat him, because Afu was old and seriously injured, he died yesterday (the 5th) morning. Deng He'er, the son of the deceased, reported it to the responsible public security branch, which sent police to arrest the murderer Zhou Yaoting and related persons Zhu Xigen and Li Yongyuan. They were presented to the general bureau and transferred to the local court for trial at 3:00 PM.

In the Hupu area, more than ten catties of white sugar can be exchanged for one national currency dollar. It is heard that these smuggled goods are transferred from Baimao Port. There are several merchants in that area who have formed a group and specially hired sandboats to transport goods from Lushun and Dalian. The goods are rayon, white sugar, matches, and newsprint. Before the establishment of the Hebei-Chahar Political Council, these merchants had already started their activities, so the amount of their transportation is impossible to estimate. After the ship docked, the passenger looked flustered. Yang Zhicai, a customs tax police officer from Zhenhai Customs, found him suspicious and stepped forward to interrogate him. After searching him, he found 902 yuan of foreign silver in his handbag and luggage without a pass. He was considered to be smuggling, so the person and the silver were taken to the customs for disposal. Water Police Shot and Killed Pirates 99

The Water Police Third Detachment stationed in Xiangshan has been patrolling the waters of Sanmen Bay for days to protect fishermen. Recently, they received a secret report from fishermen that a robbery occurred in the waters of Tianwan. They immediately rushed to the scene of the incident to pursue and suppress. They encountered a pirate ship full of pirates. The two sides fought fiercely for several hours. The pirates raised their sails and tried to escape. The patrol ship followed closely and chased them to the waters of Huazhi Mountain. They shot and killed six pirates, and the rest abandoned the boat and landed ashore. In addition to reporting the arrest of the bandits to the headquarters, they rescued three refugees and seized two rifles and more than 70 rounds of ammunition.
