Zhou Hengyun Accused of Rape and Abandonment by Concubine 158

Zhou Hengyun, a native of Ningbo working as an accountant at the Yuantai Heng Sugar Store at No. 15 Fujian Road in the French Concession, is 35 years old this year. He married a woman surnamed Qiu from his hometown. Ms. Qiu had a younger sister, Qiu Gengli, who is 23 years old this year. Because she often visited her sister, she frequented Zhou's house. Zhou found his wife's younger sister attractive and young. Around 1933, he used every means to first seduce Gengli into a sexual relationship. Then, he persuaded his father-in-law to take her as a concubine. He rented a house at No. 2 Guifu Lane, Guangqi Road in the city, to live with her, and later moved to No. 18 Yongri Lane on the same road. Recently, Zhou suddenly changed, developing a desire for novelty and aversion to the old. Using the excuse that Gengli had not borne any children since living with him, he first frequently scolded her, then even abused and beat her, driving her out and abandoning her. Qiu Gengli, feeling that her reliance had been betrayed and unable to endure it any longer, since Zhou worked at the Yuantai Heng Sugar Store in the French Concession, hired a lawyer to file a suit with the Criminal Court of the Special No. 2 Court. She accused Zhou Hengyun of rape and abandonment, requesting that he be investigated under Articles 221 and 293 of the Criminal Law. She also filed a private suit to recover ten years of living expenses calculated at 50 yuan per month, as well as 500 yuan in cash and a set of gold jewelry worth 800 yuan, including a gold bracelet, three gold rings, and one gemstone ring, which she had been defrauded of. Upon receiving the lawsuit, the court, yesterday, had Criminal Court President Wang Gangxu preside over a hearing in the Second Criminal Court. The defendant did not appear. The plaintiff, Qiu Gengli, urged her lawyer to present the case. The court first asked about the plaintiff's age and origin, then instructed that the court had dispatched police to serve a summons on the defendant. It was stated that he was currently in Ningbo, not in Shanghai, and no one had received the summons. Then, the plaintiff testified about how she was forced into becoming Zhou's concubine and the process of her being abandoned. The court stated that the location of the defendant's crime of cohabitation with the plaintiff was in the Chinese territory and thus was outside its jurisdiction. It should be prosecuted in the Shanghai District Court. After the statement, the court ruled that the case was outside its jurisdiction and adjourned.

Report on the Good Deeds of the Pushan Villa in May 164

In May 1936, the Shanghai Pushan Villa collected and buried 251 large coffins and 3,209 small coffins in both the Northern and Southern Chinese Concessions. It provided 1,517 coffins of various sizes, including 12 large coffins and 1,927 small coffins collected by the main villa. The Xieqiao and Nanshi branches, as well as various charitable halls in the French Concession, collected 473 small coffins. The Public Concession police stations and the Health Department consulted on the disposal of abandoned infant corpses and unclaimed bodies from various hospitals in the morgue, collecting 111 large coffins and 744 small coffins. The Red Cross Society's Haig Road First Hospital collected 3 large coffins. Tongren Hospital collected 1 large coffin. Renji Hospital collected 1 large coffin. Lianyi Charity Association collected 3 large coffins and 24 small coffins. The Health Bureau consulted on the burial of floating corpses from the Nanshi Rihui Port, collecting 117 large coffins and 41 small coffins. Jisheng Association collected 1 large coffin. All of the above bodies were collected by the villa's vehicles and transported to the Yidi cemetery in Dachang Tangqiao for burial, with markers set up for claiming. The Shanghai North Railway Station Xinmin Road White Cross Pushan Maternity Hospital provided diagnoses and medications to a total of 3,143 patients.

Special Article

The Meaning of the National Flag and the Public's Understanding 166

— Wu Tiecheng

The national flag is the embodiment of the national spirit and the symbol of national personality

Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, in his speech on the meaning of the national flag in Chengdu last year, proclaimed to our people: "The national flag is not only the sacred symbol representing the nation, but also the place where the spirit and life of our entire nation, from our ancestors the Yellow Emperor to us and to our descendants for thousands of generations, are gathered." He also said that the national flag of the Blue Sky, White Sun, and Red Earth is a symbol of the total life of our Chinese nation passed down in one continuous line from the Yellow Emperor. It is also the trust of the souls of our Republic of China, our ancestors since the Yellow Emperor, our Premier, and the revolutionary martyrs, and the gathering place of the common faith of our 400 million compatriots. Therefore, if we want to respect our ancestors and love our country, we must respect the national flag and love the national flag. When we see the national flag, it is equal to seeing our country and our ancestors, as well as the revolutionary martyrs who sacrificed for the revolution from the Premier down, and we must be solemn and respectful and rise up in excitement to continue to maintain in our hands and carry forward the national life and culture of our ancestors for five thousand years, save our country, and revive our nation, so that the national flag will forever fly in the world. Therefore, if we want to respect our country, we should love our national flag. If we want to express the spirit of respecting the country and loving the country, we should start with respecting the national flag and loving the national flag. Citizens of all countries have great respect for their national flags and take great care of them. Therefore, their national concept and national consciousness are very developed, and the people of their countries are able to love, cooperate, unite, and strive together for the benefit and glory of the nation under a unified banner. Looking at our country, the general public not only does not know how to respect and love the national flag, but also does not know what the national flag is, resulting in the people of the whole country having no central faith, no unified will, and no spirit of unity. They are mostly selfish and do not know how to strive for the survival and development of the country. Therefore, if we want to save the country from its difficulties and revive the nation, we must actively cultivate the national concept and national consciousness of the people. To seek the development of the national concept and national consciousness, we must start with respecting the national flag and loving the national flag. This city is the area where national culture is most developed, and the public's understanding of the national flag is especially important to both Chinese and foreign observers. Therefore, the people of this city should have a correct understanding of the design and meaning of the national flag, especially at ordinary times, so as to fully promote the spirit of our Republic of China.

The Hardware Industry in Shanghai, Compiled by China Credit Information Agency 167

(A General Overview of Shanghai's Industry and Commerce, No. 27)

Business and Overview - Since most hardware products are imported, operators must order from the managing foreign firms of various countries in this port. When placing orders, there are no samples, and past styles are used as the standard. This is because countries pay close attention to the standardization of goods. For example, if a product from a certain factory in a certain country is ordered, there should be no major errors if the name of the goods is clearly stated. The weight of the goods is mostly calculated in tons, or in grosses (twelve dozen), or in boxes. The market price is calculated according to the currency system of each country, so there is a risk of fluctuations in exchange rates. Freight and insurance are mostly calculated and paid by the foreign firm, or added to the value at the time of ordering. After the order arrives in port, the purchasing foreign firm submits a notification form to collect the goods. The payment of the goods is made by exchanging the bill of lading for a bank draft with a term of ten days from the arrival of the goods. The above is a general description of ordering from foreign firms. If it is a domestic product, then the factory or managing merchant mostly sends personnel to directly solicit business. As for the sales of goods, both local and out-of-town sales are equally important. Local sales mostly employ runners to negotiate transactions, while out-of-town sales are conducted by letter or telegram. Transportation costs are borne by the customer, and insurance is paid by the seller. If there is a Shanghai Customs declaration, the goods only need to be delivered to the port of loading, and the customer's customs broker will count the goods. The shipping and insurance costs do not need to be paid on behalf of the customer. However, the price of the goods is of course somewhat cheaper than those not handled by Shanghai Customs declarations. Payment of accounts is mostly at the end of the month, whether large or small, but there are also terms of ten or twenty days. Payment of out-of-town accounts is mostly made by a draft with a term of ten days from the arrival of the goods. Occasionally, accounts are cleared in three installments or once a month. If handled by Shanghai Customs declarations, payment can be collected the day after the goods are shipped. If the goods do not match the original sample, or the price is more expensive than other companies, the goods can be returned or the price can be reduced, commonly known as "cutting the price." As for bidding for business from administrative agencies and private homes, the profits are meager and funds must be advanced. The measurement of goods when selling, except for fixed amounts, is generally calculated according to the market scale, but there are also those who still use the Sima scale (i.e., the weighing scale). The annual turnover of each industry varies greatly, with some having the lowest turnover. Among them, the copper and tin industry has a large turnover because the market price of copper and tin raw materials is high, with the highest reaching over one million yuan, and the middle level being six or seven hundred thousand yuan to one million yuan. Next is the small hardware industry! Generally, from 300,000 yuan to 1.2 million yuan. The next is the large hardware industry, with large ones reaching one million yuan and medium ones four or five hundred thousand yuan. The least is the iron industry, because the value of steel is low, so its turnover is about 890,000 yuan at the highest and 230,000 yuan at the lowest. Most of the hardware stores in Shanghai are located along the street, except for the copper and tin industry. The copper and tin stores that are open to the public sell finished household copper and tin utensils such as kitchenware. (To be continued)

National Children's Painting Exhibition Opening Tomorrow Morning at the Sports Field; Grand Reception for All Sectors Held Last Night 174

The Shanghai National Children's Painting Exhibition held a reception yesterday at 7 PM at the Zhimei Building for various sectors of the city. The preparatory committee, led by Municipal Education Bureau Director Pan Gongzhan, personally hosted the event and reported on the significance of holding the children's painting exhibition. Details are as follows:

Welcoming Guests The invitees included representatives from *Shen Bao*, *Shishi Xinbao*, *Continental Times*, *Li Bao*, *Da Wan Bao*, *Da Mei Wan Bao*, *The Times*, *Xinwen Bao*, *Ta Kung Pao*, *Chung Hua Jih Pao*, *Min Bao*, *Central Daily News*, *Da Gong She*, *Kuomintang News Agency*, as well as government officials such as Zhu Fengwei, Lu Shuping, and Wu Liguo from the Municipal Government, Wu Liguo, Director of the Chinese Health Bureau of the Public Concession, Chen Heqin from the Chinese Education Department of the Public Concession, Chen Gongsu, Jiang Jianbai, Hu Shuyi, Ma Chong, and Shao Rugan from the Municipal Education Bureau, Hu Baomin and Xu Wangyun from the Zhejiang Education Department, Yan Kechang and Ma Gongyu from the China Art Education Society, and Chen Tiesheng from the China Child Welfare Association.

Director Pan's Speech During the dinner, Director Pan delivered a speech, briefly stating his gratitude for the presence of guests from all sectors. He emphasized that the children's painting exhibition was a pioneering initiative aimed at researching and promoting children's painting, inspiring artistic interest, and improving art education. He mentioned that various provinces and cities had submitted exhibits to the committee for display, and he hoped that all sectors would attend and provide guidance to facilitate continuous improvement. He further emphasized that the primary criterion for selecting exhibits was to ensure they were genuinely created by the children themselves, to uphold the true meaning of the event.

Provincial and Municipal Representatives Besides art school students assisting with the arrangements, representatives from various provinces and cities were responsible for the internal layout of the venue. These included Shen Elou and Fu Boliang from Jiangsu Province, Shi Wenbin and Zhu Shiqin from Nanjing City, Hubei Province, and Jiangxi Province, Yan Keding from Henan, Fujian, Shanxi, and Shandong provinces, Tan FuKai from Hunan and Anhui provinces and Qingdao City, and Zhu YunSong from Shanghai City and Suiyuan Province, Jidang Province, Hu Baoliang etc. Guangdong Zhu YunSong etc.

Opening Tomorrow Morning The opening ceremony will be held at 9 AM tomorrow at the Municipal Stadium. Mrs. Wu, the Mayor's wife, will perform the ribbon-cutting ceremony, followed by the official opening. The exhibition will last for ten days, and all sectors are welcome to visit. Primary school students can contact Chen Jiaju of the Municipal Public Utilities Bureau's Fourth Section to arrange visits, specifying the number of students and the desired time, so that they can travel by public bus, with a limit of fifty people per bus.

Yan Kechang, a member of the preparatory committee and head of the judging panel, shared his views with reporters yesterday as follows:

Initial Proposal In recent years, Chinese society has gradually paid attention to children's affairs because children are the seeds of the nation's continuous life. Whether children's education is good or bad is related to the rise and fall of the nation's future. Therefore, the government created the National Children's Year to awaken the people's attention to children's affairs. Many undertakings for the welfare of children have been held for one year. The China Art Education Society believes that children's paintings can cultivate children's temperament, inspire children's thoughts, and cultivate children's creativity, so it is recommended to hold a national children's painting exhibition. The second is to test the state of children's psychological activities and learn about their intelligence, which is the basis for the implementation of all children's education. After being passed, six related organizations and departments jointly prepared.

Exhibition Theme The purpose of this children's painting exhibition has two points: (1) to inspire children's artistic interest, cultivate aesthetic instincts, and give play to creative nature; (2) to study children's artistic tendencies, test imagination ability, and help improve children's education. Based on the above principles, the painting exhibition is purely for testing and research purposes, and there is absolutely no merit test and competition. The quality of the products has no honor or disgrace relationship with children's teachers and parents, so at the beginning of the collection of products, I am deeply afraid that they are still trapped in long-term habits and still strive to be strange, so I have repeatedly stated that the selected products should pay full attention to children's creations.

Review Opinions The exhibits from all parties are based on a province and city as a unit, and the score is used to observe the artistic tendencies of the place. By the end of the review, there were 28 units, and the amount of products was about 1,000 pieces. Although the quantity of products varies greatly, products from remote provinces and regions have participated. At the time of review, we still adhere to a consistent proposition, and those who do not meet the standards will not be accepted, and those who are not made by students will not be accepted. As a result of the review, one-third of the selected products are counted. Now, the common opinions of the reviewers are divided into two items, and several points are put forward as follows: (A) Points that meet the standards: (1) Young students and lower grades, middle-grade students are more lively and interesting. (2) A few places can still exert local characteristics. (3) Some of the products have new life education significance or national ideological performance. (B) Points that do not meet the standards: (1) The teaching methods in a few places are still outdated, and the materials are mostly imitations of popular styles. (2) There are too many copies and retouching or works instructed by adults, which lose children's pure creative nature. (3) Lack of local teaching materials.

Too Few Works The above points are just general observations. As for the precise opinions, they should be the results of the evaluation. However, the number of educated children in the country is more than 12.22 million. The detailed rules for collecting goods from this meeting originally stipulated that five creative works should be selected from every 100 children. It is estimated that the number of products in the country should be more than 500,000, but the number of products is less than one-tenth, which proves that the art of our country has not been popularized, and there are still a few units that have not produced any products so far, which is really beyond our expectations.

Municipal Education Bureau Formulates Supplementary Examination Measures for Entrance Examination Students; Measures for Entrusting Supplementary Examinations in Various Provinces and Cities Also Announced Yesterday 176

Notice from the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau: This semester's graduation entrance examinations for middle schools and normal schools have been revised regarding the examination subjects according to Instruction No. 5244 of the Ministry of Education. The Bureau has complied with the revision and has separately formulated and announced the measures for this semester's graduation entrance examinations for middle schools and normal schools in this city. Regarding students from previous sessions in this city who failed one or two subjects in the entrance examination, and students from various provinces and cities who entrusted the Bureau to conduct supplementary examinations for one or two subjects, the subjects they failed may or may not be the same as the subjects in this year's entrance examination. To facilitate their participation in this year's entrance examination, the following measures are formulated separately:

(1) For students from previous sessions in this city who failed one or two subjects in the entrance examination, if the subjects for supplementary examination are exactly the same as all the subjects in this year's entrance examination, students from senior high schools, junior high schools, and normal schools should participate in the examination for each respective subject in this year's graduation entrance examination. If the subjects for supplementary examination are not included in this year's entrance examination (such as Party Principles), or are not exactly the same as all the subjects in this year's examination (such as History vs. History and Geography, Chemistry vs. Physics and Chemistry), they shall be allowed to follow the precedent of the first semester of this year, and each school shall be responsible for conducting the supplementary examination and report the results for approval. (2) For students from various provinces and cities who entrusted the Bureau to conduct supplementary examinations for one or two subjects, the Bureau will separately schedule the supplementary examinations for July 27th and 28th. However, students who need to take supplementary examinations in this city should report to the Bureau before July 15th to go through the supplementary examination procedures. This is hereby announced for compliance.

Camp Regulations (1) Each participating camp must have at least 18 people; otherwise, it will not be counted. (2) Participants must comply with the General Assembly's orders, notices, and camp discipline. (3) Participants must work and rest according to the camp's schedule. (4) The campsite will be designated by the General Assembly, and participants may not change it freely. (5) Each troop must use natural materials to decorate the campsite and build a camp gate. (6) The camp will be notified by the General Assembly at all times. (7) The raising and lowering of the national flag at the campsite will be handled by the General Assembly, and each troop does not need to hold separate ceremonies. (8) Morning exercises should be conducted by each troop on its own according to the specified time. (9) Each troop's cooking must be done behind the troop's tents, and fire safety must be observed. (10) In case of illness, the medical team must be notified immediately. (11) In case of fire, the fire brigade must be notified immediately. (12) At least one person must be assigned to guard each tent. (13) Camp security will be assigned by the General Assembly, and Boy Scouts from each troop will take turns on guard duty and patrol. Those assigned must fulfill their duties. (14) Each troop must have a troop leader or trainer in the camp to be responsible for management. (15) All camp work must be done by the Boy Scouts themselves and may not be done by servants or workers. (16) During the camp period, mutual stealing of camps is strictly prohibited. (17) Urinating and defecating anywhere, and dumping sewage and garbage, is prohibited. (18) Public items in the camp and trees and crops around the camp must be protected. If there is any damage, compensation will be required. (19) During the camp period, each troop may not arbitrarily send signals specified by the General Assembly. (20) Each troop must break camp after the awards ceremony at the General Assembly's closing ceremony.

Inspection Instructions 1. Each troop must have at least 18 people participating in the inspection; otherwise, it will not be counted. 2. Each troop will be organized into a squad of nine people (including the platoon leader). 3. Each troop is limited to one leader. 4. The troop leader of each troop must be arranged in the line, whether in a horizontal or vertical formation. The troop flag does not need to be carried. 5. In addition to the squad, each troop should have a troop flag bearer, without a flag guard. 6. Except for the designated band in the vicinity, each troop's band does not need to be carried. 7. During the parade, the troop flag is to the right of the troop leader or in the assembly field. During the march, the troop flag is in front of the troop leader. 8. All kinds of exercises are based on the elementary curriculum compiled and printed by the former Central Training Department. 9. During the inspection, Boy Scouts in each troop must roll up their sleeves above the elbow. 10. During the inspection, backpacks, axes, canteens, and food bags do not need to be carried.

World Games: Compilation of Track and Field Results from Previous Sessions (Part 1) 178

— Huai

The 11th World Games will be held in Berlin, Germany, from August 1st to 16th this year. China has shown great determination this time, sending so many athletes to participate, and also sending two inspection teams to Germany for observation. This makes us extremely happy. The football team has already gone abroad in advance, and the basketball team has also undergone a long period of joint training. Track and field competitions first opened training classes in Beiping, creating many excellent records. Now the best players in the country have gathered in Shanghai and will hold national preliminary rounds at Shen Garden in the next two days. At least twelve strong players will be selected to attend the World Games. During this period, the entire sports community is paying close attention to this preliminary round. If the results of the previous World Games are sorted out and classified during this period for the country's athletes, sports experts, and the public to see, I think it will be more practical and meaningful than any timely article. Here we can see how the results of the first few World Games were, how the results of the recent World Games are, and how the world's competitive world has progressed. At the same time, we can make a self-comparison, confirm our confidence, and move forward. We are not without hope.

The World Games are held every four years. From 1896 when French expert Coupe Tin revived Greek literature to the present, it is exactly the 40th anniversary. A total of ten sessions have been held. However, in 1906, due to a special invitation from the Greek government, a special meeting was held in Greece. Many European countries did not participate. That is, the countries that participated, the players sent were not the best members of the country. Therefore, this meeting is not calculated in the number of official World Games. The 6th Congress was originally scheduled to be held in Germany in 1916. At that time, it was under the raging flames of Europe, and it did not open. In fact, the World Games have only been held nine times. The Berlin meeting this year is the tenth time, because the sixth session was not held, this should also be explained.

The following results regarding the track and field event section are all in feet, because a book I am based on is a report from the Canadian Olympic Committee attending the 9th World Games in the Netherlands in 1929. The track and field results of each session in this book are all in feet. I have not found any other books using "meters", so I can only base it on the Canadian report and calculate it in "feet".

In addition, the original English names of the winning athletes in each event in each session are deleted and not used, and all are translated according to the transliteration. Fortunately, our main purpose is to look at his results, and the name is secondary.

Special Issue Celebrating Teachers' Day

My Hopes for Teachers 179

— Pan Gongzhan

Teachers' Day comes around once again each year. As teachers across the nation rejoice and celebrate, I have two hopes.

First, I hope that teachers will pay more attention to cultivating their character. We know that a sound teaching staff not only needs to possess abundant knowledge but, especially, needs to have a complete character. Only with excellent character can they gain the faith of students and the sympathy of society. On the occasion of celebrating Teachers' Day, I hope that teachers will examine themselves more closely and strive to cultivate a teaching staff with excellent character.

Second, I hope that teachers will continuously pursue further studies. Because society is progressing day by day, and new knowledge is increasing day by day. If they do not continue to study, they will soon become outdated. Therefore, teachers should read more books and newspapers in their spare time and must work harder on subjects related to themselves. General knowledge should not be neglected either. If teachers can pursue further studies in this way, they can always stand at the forefront of the times.

Holding Teachers' Day on this day of serious national crisis has even greater significance. I hope that teachers will not only be a sound teaching staff but also become the vanguard of national revival.

The Mission of Today's Teachers 180

— Chen Gongsu

The quality of a country's education is related to the rise and fall of a country. On the one hand, it cannot be separated from the enlightenment of knowledge. On the other hand, it should pay more attention to spiritual training. The responsibility of enlightening knowledge and training the spirit lies with the teachers. Therefore, the quality of education depends on whether the teachers can fulfill their mission.

Today's China is in trouble. There is nothing worse. Internal worries have not been eliminated, and external insults are becoming more urgent. Crises are lurking on all sides, and the national crisis is deepening. However, the vast majority of the population is still not aware of it. Many people are ignorant and do not know the relationship between individuals and the country. They only know about personal interests and do not know about national interests. Those who would rather sacrifice national interests to preserve their personal interests are everywhere. The decline of national consciousness is so serious that it is truly worrying. However, the function of education is used to transform the people's psychology, thereby promoting national consciousness, so as to save the country from subjugation, which has also become the most urgent need today.

In terms of the tasks of teachers, their teaching and training work has the highest value, and the importance of training is even above teaching. Teaching means imparting knowledge and enlightening knowledge. Academics rely on it to flourish, culture relies on it to advance, and the level of the people relies on it to improve. It is extremely important for a country's future, and its importance goes without saying. Training is to shape personality and train the spirit. Its purpose is to enable trainees to develop noble character and great aspirations. Its impact is enough to change the quality of the people and change customs. Those who have talent but lack virtue often contribute less to society and the country than those who have more virtue than talent. Those who are willing to sacrifice national interests are not all incompetent. It is just that they lack virtue. Therefore, those who are responsible for education, it is better to train people who are more virtuous than talented than to train people who are more talented than virtuous.

Now, the teachers in the school, at this time of crisis, are serving in the education sector, which is really called "heavy responsibility and a long way to go". The results of their work are closely related to the future of the nation. Therefore, teachers who work hard in their positions are repaying society. In addition to hoping that society will recognize the importance of teachers' status and obtain job security, I also hope that all teachers should make the greatest determination, embrace the spirit of sacrifice, and devote themselves to education. Teach people with an attitude of learning without getting tired of teaching, train people with the spirit of "setting an example", and use educational methods to achieve the goal of transforming society. If they can achieve their goals, the results of their efforts can enable the project of saving the country and achieving survival to be completed as soon as possible, and the future of our nation can be expected. It is not just to create excellent young people.

Celebrating Teachers' Day and Promoting the Literacy Education Movement 182

— Jiang Jianbai

So-called literacy education, also education to eliminate illiteracy, is completely for adults who have missed out on schooling. It differs from remedial education in that those who receive remedial education have attended school and need to make up for some special knowledge. Those who receive literacy education have not attended school and need to make up for general literacy and common sense guidance for civic training. Therefore, literacy education is equal to primary school education for adults.

China is economically backward and culturally backward, so there are especially many illiterate people. They cannot read newspapers and books, which is extremely inconvenient for anti-imperialist propaganda. Also, because they cannot read newspapers and books and have no knowledge, their worldview is narrow and they are indifferent to politics, resulting in the dispersal of national power and difficulty in concentrating it. Therefore, eliminating illiteracy and raising their cultural standards is undoubtedly very important.

Now, all parts of the country are working hard on literacy education and eliminating illiteracy. We, as teachers, in addition to being loyal to our own duties, should actively advocate, publicize, sponsor, and serve such literacy education work that meets the needs of the country, in order to complete the popularization of education as soon as possible.

National Crisis Education and Teachers 183

— Chen

Who does not know that 1936 is a very special period? In this special period, the issue of special education has attracted the attention of people in the education sector across the country. National crisis education is not to create a special education outside the country's entire education, but to add to or subtract from the original education that has not achieved results in dealing with the national crisis for a hundred years, focusing on what is urgent so that it can fully exert the function of saving the country from the crisis. In other words, "education that consumes national power does not meet the needs of the national crisis period, and education that cultivates national power deserves to be called national crisis education." The key points of education during the national crisis have been clearly instructed by Minister Wang of the Ministry of Education, one is physical training, the second is spiritual training, and the third is special knowledge and skills training. Under this "national crisis education", we, as teachers, can work even harder day and night to achieve the salvation of the national crisis and the revival of the nation.

— Feng Yixian

Since the September 18th Incident, the national crisis has become increasingly serious. Now, it has reached an extraordinary period of national crisis and survival. Shanghai Educational Association: A Respectful Message to All Teachers in the City on Teachers' Day 185

Another year has passed, and it is once again Teachers' Day in the 25th year of the Republic. Teachers' Day was established by our colleagues in the education sector because the treatment of teachers in our country is extremely meager, to the point where individual food and clothing problems cannot be resolved, let alone the plans for supporting parents and raising children. Their lives are extremely difficult. However, the responsibilities they bear are to instill knowledge in students, cultivate the character of children, and build the foundation for national rejuvenation, strengthening the nation, and wiping out humiliation. The weight of responsibility can be said to be extreme.

The responsibility is so heavy, and the treatment is so meager. Therefore, our colleagues in the education sector established Teachers' Day to awaken society's attention and sympathy. On the one hand, it allows teachers to have this opportunity to gather together and learn from each other's strengths and weaknesses, review past achievements, reflect on past gains and losses, and decide on future directions for educational reform. Strive for self-cultivation in scholarship and morality, in order to establish an excellent example for teachers. Then the meaning of establishing this holiday can be known, and it is not just holding ceremonies. Therefore, I do not presume to be humble and respectfully offer a word to serve as a congratulatory message. I hope you will take it into consideration.

(1) Education is the foundation of a nation. With the widespread popularization of education, the level of knowledge of the people is high, and the love of country is strong. Countries in the East and the West strive to enrich educational funding, but our country is the opposite. Therefore, the education cause is on the verge of collapse. This kind of phenomenon relies on our teachers to find ways to remedy it. The way to remedy it is to endure hardship, actively struggle, and make educational achievements new every day, in order to arouse the faith and worship of people in society. If this is the case, then the fundraising for education funding will be easy, and the goal of popularizing education will be achieved. This is the first point to teach our colleagues.

(2) Han Yu said, "Teachers are the ones who impart the Tao, teach skills, and resolve doubts." It can be seen that being a teacher is not only about teaching students to read, but also about enabling students to know the way to establish themselves in the world, learn extensively, inquire carefully, think prudently, discern clearly, understand etiquette, know integrity, be responsible, and abide by discipline. Therefore, the future teaching policy must focus on imparting the Tao, teaching skills, and resolving doubts, and not just recite chapters and sentences. This is the second point to teach our colleagues.

(3) In the past, teachers mostly regarded teaching students to read as their best effort. Therefore, students often found themselves at a loss when they left school and entered society. Therefore, teachers should not only teach reading, but also give them opportunities for practice and self-government, cultivate the habit of diligence, the spirit of courage, the will of perseverance, the integrity of character, be quick in doing things and careful in methods, so that they can cope with ease when they enter society in the future and not have the problem of incompetence in everything. Learning is for application, so that we will not go against the purpose of education. This is the third point to teach our colleagues.

(4) The environment in which our country is currently located is extremely dangerous and evil, crises are everywhere, and it is a matter of life and death. The education policy should be adapted to the circumstances. Military training and military management in secondary and higher schools have profound meaning. In the future, we must inspire students' patriotic ideas, focus on military education, believe in the Three Principles of the People, obey the orders of the leader, and cultivate the spirit of hard work, perseverance, and indomitable spirit. This is the fourth point to teach our colleagues.

The above discussion is just a foolish idea. I hope my colleagues will encourage each other and hope that all colleagues will express great opinions and further teach them, then it will be fortunate.

Shen Bao Literary Supplement

Companion 187

— Zi Gang

In the evening, dragging a tired body, I returned from work. The spring sun set so early, and I felt that the noisy and cramped residence was filled with cold. But when I rang the bell, a layer of joy floated in my heart: Has Kaka Biankaf returned? My foreign neighbor whom I had known for less than half a month.

The landlady opened the door with a mouthful of opium smoke. Because I had paid her the rent that had been in arrears for a week yesterday, her face was a little better today, and I was a little more dignified, unlike the past few days when I was dodging like a demon with huge claws stretched out.

"Has the gentleman in the pavilion room on the third floor returned?" I couldn't help but ask.

"Oh, that Russian devil, moved away, it was cheap for him for ten days' rent..."

My empty right hand rested on her thin shoulder, almost patting it hard, and I cursed in my heart: Opium addict, you are good, it's all you who made him go!

She paused and glared: "What's wrong, treat them the same, I can't let him live in a house without paying!"

"You should have told me first!" I finally blurted out, the red tide on my face receding.

"Oh, I forgot, he left a note for you in my tobacco shop." She turned around to get it.

I returned to my pavilion room, too late to light the lamp, and hastily unfolded the short note Kaka left me in the dim light in front of the window.

On the paper was a burning heart, two eyes filled with tears.

He apologized to me, thanked me, and wished me good health. Finally, he said he would never forget the only ray of pale friendship I had given him in the contempt and ridicule he had suffered in his exiled life.

Finally, he begged me to forgive his sudden escape, which was really because he was being forced too hard, and also mentioned the few times I had helped him with money, which made him feel guilty and ashamed.

"Maybe you will run into me on any street corner, but I will run away from you far away, so that you won't feel uncomfortable seeing me." His sentences were written very briefly, so that I could understand. He could write beautiful characters of his homeland, and like this clear and decadent wanderer, those characters were just gentle and lacked a bit of vitality.

I read the short note repeatedly, as if trying to find other sentences: or one day he would move back and be a warm neighbor again—we were neighbors separated by a floor, each occupying a pavilion room. He could hear my long-term coughing, and I could hear his anxious footsteps at midnight.

However, there was nothing else on the white paper. I only seemed to see that pair of gray, deep-set eyes gazing, and a long sigh flew out of the helpless gaze.

I picked up the Russian story collection that Kaka had lent me. It was full of simple little stories that could make people smile. Every night Kaka taught me to read one. He was so serious, correcting my pronunciation and explaining the grammar. When I could never roll my tongue to read a "ba" sound, he was anxiously scratching his hair. When I made the sentence smooth, he would pat me on the shoulder and say, "Very good."

He could also speak a little simple Shanghai dialect. I first met him in front of a small fruit shop. It was morning, and when I walked past the shop, I only heard some shop assistants laughing:

"Can't afford to buy, don't buy!"

"Poor devil, foreign ghost!"

Jian Kaka stood silently in front of the fruit stall, his eyes fixed on a pile of small and coarse oranges that cost one copper coin each. He groped in the pockets of his snuff-colored worn-out suit, his eyes as heavy as if they were dead.

Gently, he pinched out two copper coins with his left hand, dodging the ridicule of the shop assistants in the air, and carefully picked two and left.

Even the passers-by nearby laughed, but this strange friend walked away without turning his head, his slender, slightly hunched shadow reflected on the wall.

Not many days later, in the evening, when I returned from outside and walked past the door of the landlady's room, the slender figure was unexpectedly in front of me again.

I was stunned, and he seemed startled, then turned his head away shyly.

I finally heard clearly that the landlady was asking him for rent.

"Fu you lari," he patted his pocket and added a sentence in his own language: "Niet, niet!" (No, no!)

It turned out that he and I had been unknown neighbors for more than a month.

When he finished the negotiation, we met by the escalator. When he found out that I had also studied their language for a few months, he laughed lively and forced me to speak his language with grammatical errors.

We used loneliness and mutual poverty to make friendship, often telling each other about our fatigue. I always encouraged him with the enthusiasm of a young man growing in the thorny road. Sometimes he would抿抿嘴角, sometimes - especially when talking about his new motherland, he always shook his head. He said he also knew it was an unprecedented paradise, but...

Is it the airs of a gentleman?

"It always seems like it belongs to me—"

I refuted him with a kind smile. He allowed that one day he would拍拍掉 this old yoke and step into a new home, a new motherland.

But for the time being, he still ran out every two or three days to find his old companions who were more comfortable than him and get some financial assistance to live on. Occasionally, he would take out a few cents and tell me that he had earned it through work, but he didn't say how he worked, but he always passionately said to me:

"You work hard, work can make people forget their worries!"

I put down this farewell note and opened the story collection. I don't know when he had secretly written a few lines on the title page, and finally crookedly塗着 a few big characters:

"Kaka to Axiao."

These Chinese characters were what I had taught him to write under the lamp while holding his hand.

Before Sunset 188

— Wen Ruo

——Sketch of a Wharf——

The lake, as if unable to bear the excessive loneliness, quietly danced with her light green clothes; the golden ball-like sun was about to fall on the roof of the "Yue Wang Temple." The wharf was densely packed with rows of yellow and black boats. Looking from a distance, only a few rows of irregular gray-yellow rattan chairs floated on the water, like seats in a theater, with a few dazzling white "sofas" interspersed in between, which seemed quite out of tune.

Under the willow tree by the bridge pier lay a large stone pier like a coffin, crowded with a pile of people. Everyone had even finished talking about the materials for chatting, and they were all silently gazing at the not-so-distant road, hoping that a few more customers would appear; only Jinqian, who had no family or burden and was still joking even when hungry, was pulling at the gray cloth cotton robe that was one piece of yellow and one piece of black, dancing alone like a stilt chicken, humming in his mouth: "Oh, Willow Green..." The voice was strangely shrill.

"Ugh!" Gengshui, squatting on the stone pier, raised his bark-like hand and searched his throat, pretending to be nauseous:

"Okay, okay, little devil! Listening to others singing makes your heart itch, listening to you sing only gives you goosebumps—wait a while and even your bones will be numb, it's not worth it if there's business!"

"Huh? Don't worry, there won't be any business for you to do, so listen to me sing happily!"

Jinqian stopped his feet and said a few words, then hopped and hummed again crookedly.

"Jinqian, it's a pity you have an extra thing in your crotch!" Baohe, whose forehead was engraved with "Nine Creeks and Eighteen Streams"—this was the nickname given to him by his companions—said; he聳聳顋, and the wrinkles on his forehead immediately became so deep that he couldn't see the bottom. His companions all knew; he was smiling."

"If you didn't have that thing, I guarantee you wouldn't sing" "Willow Green Willow Red, business would definitely be good!" He continued.

"Jinqian, cut it off, and Baohe guarantees your business will be good!" Gengshui jumped off the stone pier and pushed Jinqian.

"Not a face reader, that's the truth, if Daqingniang came, business would definitely be good!" Baohe put on the old senior's airs that he was used to putting on: "Hey, Jiaxing, the boats are all rowed by women, dressed up quite nicely, with gold hairpins and gold rings—we should also try this trick, I guarantee your business will be good!"

Gengshui couldn't help but 　, first chuckling softly. Jinqian only tore open his mouth and歪扯着 his face, saying:

"I'm afraid you don't have a吤 pretty wife, even if you dress her up, she'll look like a" "Old Mother—not as pretty as me!"

"Haha..." Everyone laughed.

Behind the stone pier, on the long snake-like white dike that separated the inner and outer lakes, the crisp sound of footsteps rang out.

They immediately forgot the jokes just now, stood up from the stone pier nervously, and shouted with their throats stretched out:

"Do you want a sampan? Do you want a sampan?" A group of young foreign men and women, flaunting thin tweed coats and dancing with "sticks, walking with their chests out."

"Do you want a sampan? Three dimes an hour!"

Gengshui shouted vigorously and jumped forward, holding out three fingers.

But the foreigners only chatted嗞嗞咕咕, without turning their heads, and walked straight to the bus stop.

Gengshui had to lower his head and return to the stone pier to squat.

"Foreigners seem to be poor now too, foreign business is really hard to do!" Baohe cleared his throat and put on the old senior's airs again. "It's good that they only talk about hours, they don't even use cents, one dollar is always ten cents—yesterday I rowed for one customer, three hours, I agreed on ten dollars!"

He shook his head and twisted his buttocks, as if he was still rowing such good business now.

Gengshui took off his felt hat and scratched the back of his flat head, slowly saying as if he had remembered something:

"Such good business, only you "sofa boats" do! We—"

"Sofa boat?" Baohe immediately吼起来 as if he had touched a sore spot, deeply邹起 the "Nine Creeks and Eighteen Streams" on his forehead:

"In order to install this short-lived sofa, I joined a ten-dollar club, and now I can't even pay the club fee!"

Gengshui glanced at him and still said enviously:

"It's good to have something to borrow!"

"Hey! Yes, long debts are still good!" All the smiles on his face disappeared, leaving only a face full of sullenness.

"That's it, let's talk less nonsense. It's true that you did good business yesterday, so please treat us!" Gengshui opened his mouth wide and turned the words around.

"Okay, I'll treat you, come to my house for dinner tonight and eat good dishes!" Baohe became得意起来 again, as if saying: "After all, I, Baohe, am not bad!"

"There are crucian carp and snails." He added: "Eight copper coins for small crucian carp, if you think about it, add four copper coins for green onions;鋪一批 green onions, add a few fish, it's really fragrant when焖起來!"

"Okay, agreed!" Gengshui swallowed a big mouthful of saliva: "I'll definitely come; I won't eat your rice, we'll eat sweet potatoes tonight."

"I don't have a share?" Jinqian jumped in front of Baohe.

"I'll treat you next time!" Baohe patted his shoulder like哄孩子.

At this time, half of the big sun had disappeared behind the瓦背 of "Yue Wang Temple," and a片 of gloom appeared on the lake. Two slender figures slowly moved closer to the wharf from the quiet asphalt road. They could already see clearly that the one on the right was wearing a black velvet瓜皮 hat with a red顶, and the blue robe was闪着 a縷縷的光; the one on the left was wearing a tight-fitting suit, and half of the trouser leg outside the coat was stiff like paper. They immediately woke up from their dreams and jumped off the stone pier:

"Spin down哇?"

"Do you want to call a划子?"

Gengshui agilely rushed forward:

"Sir, do you want a划子?"

"How much旗下的?" The 反應皮帽 "Sir" asked lazily.

"Three dimes, okay?"

He shook his head and immediately accelerated his pace as if逃一般. The one wearing a suit征侧着 his head and said softly:

"I think we should take the bus, these guys specialize in敲竹槓, it's unethical!"

"Sir, how much do you want咧?" Gengshui緊緊跟 in the back: "Even if you take the bus, it will cost two角大洋, just rowing you two, and there's no回头生意. If it was before, no one would row for four角子!"

"Before?" The one wearing a瓜皮 hat sneered: "Now the years are not so good!"

"That's it, sir, how much do you say?"

"Two只角子, go if you go, forget it if you don't!" He said and twisted his head

"Okay, okay! Forget it!"

Gengshui发狠地跺了一脚, and ran to the tree to解缆.

Standing next to the suit先生, he quickly指着 a boat装西式沙发的 said:

"I want this one!"

"This is not mine," Gengshui赔着笑脸: "藤椅坐 is the same格!"

"Hum, the old藤椅 boat, no! No!"

The two位先生 left arm in arm.

"沙發船么? Four只角子!" Baohe's voice送过 from the石墩上. Gengshui恨恨地望着 them, and很想一度日拳打过去, but he忍住了:

"Sir, how is it啦,说好的"

"沙发船, two只角子. 就要!"

Gengshui牵着解下来的缆,呆呆地钉着 their背影.

Suddenly,宝和从石墩上来,一面用短促声音喊着: "来来, 划你去, 沙发船" The two people正在走的前面, 回头住了脚.

宝和连忙俯下腰去解缆.

根水心里一怔, "咳,连宝和都来抢我的生意!" But, he只好冷冷地说:

"You go?——Then what are you装啥沙发!"

宝和却不在意地将破呢帽略按一按, 甩起那发典的染满了汚渍的布棉袍后摆,塞在腰上,一面坐上船,一面摇头:

"不去?他眞不肯加的,倒反大家捞个空!"

根水望着那两个客人,分坐上两面的弹簧椅上,当中小圆桌上的金色茶壶在闪光,桨一下下地摇进那鱼鳞似的水里. He心裡一急, 就直着喉咙喊:

"旗下去哇?旗下开船哩?"

这时,荣生和金钱都慢慢地走过来,收起船上摆设的藤椅, 荣生一面咕噜着:

"一天,只划得个五十个铜板!"

金钱正拆下藤椅捧向家里

"五十个?还好!老子只三十个咧!"

根水没答嘴, 咛了一把鼻涕, 往油饼似的布袄上一抹, 又撕声地喊着:

"旗下去哇?十个铜板!"

从那宽阔的柏油路边转过七八个男男女女来,都是穿着布袄的乡佬, 他马上迎着

"要不要到旗下去?"

"几个铜板一个人?" The灰黄的毡帽下加了一对耳朶套的十七八岁的小伙子问.

"算八个垃倒哩!"

"八个?"扎着黑包头的中年妇人揷进来说: "人家五个!"

"六个!六个!"

"你又来咧!" 用粗粗的雨伞柄背着一个蓝布大包袱的中年男人, 狠狠地看了那女人一眼: "就是五个,五八得四十,也快要两只角子, 走走末好哩!"

"五个就五个,依你!"

根水跟上去.

但是,那一伙人没有一个停住脚. 声音只在灰黑色的天空和浅黄色的湖面上荡了一转, 又重新折进根水自己底耳朶里.

The Useless Fig Tree 189

— Chen Zizhan

There was a fig tree,

Planted in a vineyard.

The owner came to the tree,

But never saw any fruit.

The owner scolded the gardener:

"Has it borne fruit in ten years?"

"Quickly chop it down for me!"

"Why let it occupy the land in vain?"

The gardener still deceived the owner:

"It's better to let it exist."

"Let me dig soil and fertilize it,

Please take another look at whether it is good or bad."

The owner instructed the gardener:

"Just do as you say for the time being. If it bears fruit, then so be it, otherwise you're fired too!"

The Crossroads of New Poetry 190

— Ren Jun

Although this is a world of fire and blood, although this is an unadulterated "era of poetry," although everywhere we hear fervent calls for singers of the times; what is strange is that the poetry scene in recent years has been exceptionally desolate and沉寂, giving one a sense of utter desolation.

Why is there this phenomenon? This, of course, like the decline of the entire literary scene, has its various objective and complex factors, which are difficult to exhaust in one place; however, I have always believed that New Poetry itself contains many incorrect tendencies, in other words, New Poets have intentionally or unintentionally embarked on various dead-end detours, which should at least be one of the biggest reasons for creating this phenomenon.

Okay, now let's examine and criticize those incorrect tendencies, those detours.

I remember the great Russian critic Belinsky once saying the following: "Everyone has the right to demand that a poet, at least in his poems, should pour out his heart's sorrow for unsolvable problems. A poet who ignores the masses and only sings about himself and his own affairs will not gain a single reader besides himself." What kind of era is China currently in? What are the "pressing issues of the times"? For writers (poets) who habitually pride themselves on their sensitivity, these are of course "problems" that are not problems. That being said, what cannot but cause us the greatest surprise is that at present, China has quite a few "excellent," "reputable," and "talented" poets who are still there specializing in flowers, moons, and my lover... singing praises of nature and love songs; or filling the pages with loneliness,寂寞, dreams, illusions... and specializing in expressing a kind of 末世情绪 of 无病呻吟. Obviously, these poets, constrained by the life and consciousness of their respective classes, are unable or unwilling to grasp the correct outlook on life and the world; therefore, before this great era, they cannot but become color-blind, deaf, or try their best to close their eyes and cover their ears as if nothing had happened; they have already become unable to see the disasters, persecutions, abuses... all over the land, and they are unable to hear the enemy's artillery fire and the laments and roars of the suffering masses... As a result, for them, losing love is more worthy of sorrow and heartache than losing the Northeast, 热河, or even all of China! The so-called loneliness and寂寞, which completely belong to the personal realm, are more worthy of being expressed and depicted than any suffering and disaster of the masses! You think, how can this kind of "poet who ignores the masses and only sings about himself and his own affairs" produce great works that reflect and express the times? How can they gain the sympathy and love of readers? And if there are too many poets like this, how can the poetry scene not be desolate? ...

This can be said to be an evil tendency in the content of New Poetry that should be given the most merciless blows and corrections. Secondly, in terms of form and expression, we can also find those tendencies that should also be struck and corrected.

First, there is the tendency to start from formalism and try to standardize and formalize New Poetry. Anyone who has paid a little attention to the trends in the poetry scene will know that, whether in the past or present, there have been many poets who are making a big deal out of Western-style forms or styles of poetry; as a result, many so-called sonnets, "square poems," and so on have been produced. Obviously, this is an attempt to standardize and formalize New Poetry; that is, a kind of degeneration and restoration in the New Poetry movement, a new chain and shackle. Of course, we do not oppose people paying attention to form; on the contrary, we also acknowledge that a poet has the full right to seek the most appropriate and perfect form to express a specific content; we also understand that a good poem is not only due to its rich and substantial content, but also due to its complete and beautiful appearance. However, what must be noted here is that our emphasis on form absolutely cannot surpass the principle that form is subordinate to content, or that content is superior to form. Because we always believe that if your body is healthy and beautiful, then even being naked without a thread is not a problem, and may even make your health and beauty more obvious; on the contrary, if you are a "skeleton" without flesh and blood, then even if you put on the most gorgeous clothes and apply three inches of thick makeup, people will still shy away. Moreover, to go one step further, as is generally known, a rigid and fixed format will indeed give the content the greatest束缚 and桎梏. Why did we abandon old poetry? That is because its various unreasonable restrictions and metrics do not allow us to express the thoughts and feelings of modern people. Of course, you may say that forms like the 商籁体 are not the forms of our country's old poetry, but genuine, authentic imported goods. However, you must understand that we are of course utterly opposed to the "national essence" of foot-binding and ear-piercing for Chinese women; but at the same time, we also absolutely do not approve of their "Western-style" wearing high heels and perming their hair; because in terms of "unnaturalness" and artificiality, those are originally half a pound each. In short, this attempt to standardize and formalize New Poetry, to expose the 洋鏡, is a method of cutting your feet to fit the shoes, a trick to try to use form to cover up empty content, and it will cause New Poetry, which has finally jumped out of the mud pit of old poetry, to throw itself into a new trap again.

First, there is the tendency to write poetry that is very obscure and ambiguous. In recent years, some so-called symbolist, mystic, and imagist poets have appeared on the Chinese New Poetry scene. It is said that their motivation for writing is purely to express a light and hazy sentiment, image, and momentary感興. Their works, when read, are not only full of "吗吧呀呢," making one feel like listening to foreigners speaking Chinese, or looking at a clumsy and stiff text translated from a foreign language; moreover, even if you read their entire work very carefully, you often don't know what our "profound and unfathomable poets are saying? What are they expressing, reading is equivalent to not reading (unfortunately, due to space limitations at this moment, I cannot copy out a few of their masterpieces so that everyone can concentrate on guessing what tricks our poets are playing and what kind of mysterious things they are doing). In a word, that is: their works are generally written in colloquial language; but they are exceptionally obscure and ambiguous, making people almost suspect that they are "heavenly scriptures" or the like. The production of this kind of work, perhaps our poets have their own "brilliant" explanations and arguments; but in my opinion, despite the different sects and the different patterns of each other, due to the emptiness of the content, they cannot but tumble and perform tricks in terms of form and expression in order to cover up this point, they have a blood relationship with formalists. Because in fact, as the critic Mirsky said: "Many poets try hard to make themselves incomprehensible because they have nothing worth understanding to say." Regarding this tendency in the poetry scene, Hu Shih and Liang Shiqiu have also recently specially criticized and criticized it, saying that those poems that cannot be understood are "stupid riddles" and "a decadent literary trend," and also said: "People have to speak human language, and poets also have to speak human language, and the first requirement of human language is to be clear and clear" (see Hu Shih's "Talking about 'Hu Shih Style' Poetry" and Liang's "I Also Talk About 'Hu Shih Style' Poetry" in "Free Review, Issue 22"). However, Shao Xunmei did not think so, and wrote articles refuting them in the "Ren Yan Weekly," and even further cited foreign classics, based on foreign canons, and tried his best to praise the so-called "great obscurity." However, to be fair, if obscurity is also called "greatness," then there would be too few things in the world that are not great!

The above-mentioned tendencies can be said to be three detours for New Poetry in terms of content and form. If future poetry continues to follow these detours, then I dare say that it not only has no hope of revival, but will undoubtedly run to a dead end! Therefore, I hope that those who are dedicated to the poetry movement can use their greatest strength to pull it back from those detours, whether in theory or in works!

Homesickness 191

— Xinlao

Homesickness has become a disease for me. I always miss it, and sometimes it makes me even more melancholy. When spring comes, I think of the newly green meadows in my hometown; the sound of the water river bursting; on the newly melted muddy country roads, many feet and hooves sink in and out; and the snow water on the snowy peaks flows into small fountains; it's really beautiful!

Although the spring scenery of Jiangnan is beautiful, people who drift in other places cannot get a little spring nourishment.

——The spring of my hometown is spread all over the ground, stained with the felt hearts of every traveler. When the pomegranate flowers are full of branches, summer comes. Just this heat has already made me unable to forget the peace of the past in my hometown, sitting on that misty hillside, butterflies dancing in front of my eyes, from the 山刺梅, from the dandelion, from the 山牡丹, and then flying to the purple flowers of the 山兰——butterflies, there are not none here, and they are even more beautiful; it's just that in the bias of homesickness, they reduce their color.

Leaves are falling from the roadside plane trees, it's autumn here. I think of the 龙葵 in the weeds of my hometown; when the small black berries are eaten in my mouth——what a flavorful memory, in my childhood...

And winter is coming. The big snow in my hometown is the most memorable and longing for me. The snow covers the high mountains and low thatched houses; standing in the middle of the field, it will really be like being in a boundless snow sea; the spin lifted by the fierce wind, the snow sand like waves is flying; but how much of the shadow of snow can be seen here? Very little.

Because of this, every winter, I am parched with thirst for snow, I think of the big snowflakes in my hometown like flowers.

However, the hometown I miss, that green hillside, is full of corpses; the earth is probably crying too, right? Under the cruel slaughter of ××, even sparrows are probably unable to jump freely!

Walking on the small road that I used to walk, inspecting the courtyard where I used to live... I will point and say one by one: This is the ditch where I used to fish; this is the bank where I used to pile sand; this is the pavilion where I used to sit; this is the hillside where I used to run; this is the land where I used to insert myself; this is the forest where I used to hunt birds; this is...

If such a day comes, what would I, no, what should I do? Think about it! Cry like a child? Or roll around and laugh haha?

However, this day is so distant that whenever it rains here, I will think of the sky in my hometown. For six years, it has been so陰沉, so desolate, so miserable. Like my heart, gray clouds are飄荡.

When will my hometown be sunny? When will my heart be sunny? ——I can't help but think like this all the time. Think like this.

Uncertain US Cotton Futures, Rising British Cotton Across Months, Indian Cotton Market Closed 197

Yesterday, the US cotton market opened with fluctuations of two points up or down across various months. Bullish positions were being liquidated, and domestic and foreign firms placed limit orders to buy, leading to uneven price movements for hedging. Subsequently, due to the liquidation of bullish positions and selling from the Far East, market conditions weakened. However, persistent drought in the eastern regions meant that all sales were absorbed by new speculative buying. Manufacturers were also more active in their purchases. The spread between July and October contracts narrowed slightly. When the cotton was held at 11.65 cents, the July contract was sold off. In the afternoon, bullish positions were liquidated again, coupled with local selling, further weakening the market. At closing, some short covering provided some stability. Spot prices remained unchanged, while futures prices, except for a two-point increase in July, fell by four to eight points. Recently, there has been a gradual increase in procurement, leading to a turnaround in the market. However, due to exchange rate concerns, Guangdong merchants telegraphed their principals requesting delayed transactions. If the overall situation stabilizes, sales prospects are promising. Printed fabrics enjoyed brisk sales in the spring season this year, with various factories competing to manufacture them, resulting in a doubling of output. Later, due to poor market conditions and the detrimental impact of smuggled goods in South China, sales plummeted, and prices fell sharply. "Croco" silk, previously sold for 6.60-6.70 yuan, now sells for only 5.50-5.60 yuan. Similarly, printed fabrics priced above 6 yuan now fetch only 4.70-4.80 yuan, representing a significant decline.

Grains – Small-Scale Bulls Gradually Liquidating, Flour Market Rises Initially then Declines 202

Yesterday's flour market experienced a pattern of initial gains followed by a weakening trend across various months. Foreign wheat quotations saw a slight improvement of 0.04 in Chicago and 0.10 to 0.20 in Canada. Opening prices were firm due to the slight improvement in foreign wheat prices and uncertain weather conditions. The highest price for the current month reached 3.065 yuan, with far-month contracts also rising by about 0.01 yuan. However, by the second session, small-scale bulls gradually began to liquidate their positions, causing sentiment to gradually weaken, falling by about 0.01 yuan from the highest level. The afternoon session saw sluggish trading, with factories slightly reducing their offerings, leading to a gradual easing of far-month contracts. However, the current situation is largely influenced by hedging considerations, and as the wheat season has not yet peaked, both insiders and outsiders are adopting a wait-and-see approach. Significant developments will likely be delayed until there is concrete information on supply and demand.

Wheat Futures Market Relatively Calm, Weather Still Uncertain, Buying and Selling Marked by Caution 203

Yesterday, the wheat futures market was generally calm across various months after the morning opening. As the weather remained uncertain and foreign wheat quotations saw a slight improvement of 0.10 to 0.20 yuan, both buyers and sellers adopted a cautious approach. With limited competition, price fluctuations were minimal. Regarding this year's wheat situation, the northern regions have benefited from favorable weather conditions, resulting in a better harvest than in previous years. Furthermore, the harvest time is earlier than in the southern regions. Based on this, market sentiment is likely to change during the peak delivery period. During the afternoon opening, buying interest suddenly waned, while offerings remained scarce. Near-term contracts saw a slight improvement, but trading was not very brisk, lacking vitality. Future developments will depend on the full arrival of the new wheat crop and how factory demand and sales progress.

The average estimate for US wheat production is 501,000,000 bushels for winter wheat and 236,000,000 bushels for spring wheat, roughly in line with expectations. Drought in the Northwest has a stabilizing effect on prices, but short-selling will soon have an impact. Exports from Soviet Russia are also causing some concern.

Nanjing Elects "Miss Health" 214

— Jia Wei

On the third of this month, "Miss Health of Nanjing" was chosen. The story goes that Nanjing's Ginling Women's College, recognizing that today's aesthetic focus for women should be on health rather than outward appearance, initiated the "Miss Health of Nanjing" competition. All students and faculty members had the right to vote and be elected. Seven candidates were chosen based on the number of votes received, with the top vote-getters being elected and the next thirty being named "Healthy Students." The health standards were fourfold: 1. Healthy internal organs (verified by the school doctor); 2. Correct posture (including weight); 3. Natural, non-stiff movements; 4. Active spirit and agile movements. This campaign may be a pioneering effort. Originally, everyone knew that not long ago, "frailty" was a well-known characteristic of Chinese women. In fact, it was generally believed that women with a sickly appearance were beautiful. So at that time, typical daughters of wealthy families considered delicacy and "flatness" to be the most "modern" forms of "beauty."

However, it's undeniable that for thousands of years, Chinese women were suppressed under the poisonous influence of the feudal system, resulting in the adoption of customs and decorations that were physiologically and hygienically unsound, such as foot-binding, chest-binding, tight waists, and wearing earrings and necklaces. These inherited adornments, intended to enhance beauty, unintentionally shackled them with invisible chains, restricting their freedom throughout their lives. Although after the May Fourth Movement, some women were liberated from the shackles of foot-binding and chest-binding, the general aesthetic standard still favored "seductiveness" and "delicacy"!

Originally, this aesthetic standard was shared by people in Europe and America. However, the situation is different now. The British explorer Mr. Gore once said, "We cannot judge a woman's beauty based on past aesthetic standards. In the past, beauty was defined by seductiveness, but now, healthy beauty should be the standard. Soviet women now work as hard as men, and even exercise more diligently than men to compensate for their natural physical deficiencies. Their waists and hips are well-proportioned, and their legs and arms are full and strong. Their skin tone is between white and red, and they do not wear makeup, fully expressing natural beauty. Their lifestyle is simpler than that of European and American women, which is their only merit. Therefore, there is no doubt that Soviet women are considered the most beautiful women in the world."

However, today, young women should not only free themselves from the sickly appearance of the past and acquire a healthy and beautiful physique, but also remember the greater social responsibilities they should assume as modern women. Otherwise, they will simply become beautiful but useless shells!

Ms. Pan Yuliang's Art Exhibition 215

— Wu Shutian

The fine rain fell densely, gradually growing heavier. I greatly enjoyed such rainy days, and the long-awaited art exhibition of Ms. Pan, which opened today, made it imperative for me to brave the rain. Thinking that I needed two companions to see the art exhibition, I invited Mr. and Mrs. Fu Xue.

The venue was the China Arts and Crafts Society on Avenue Edward VII. The road was quiet, and there was no ostentation. Usually, there are many large white cloths hanging horizontally and vertically on the streets when an exhibition opens, but I didn't see any today. Only a horizontal cloth at the entrance of the venue was wet from the rain.

Seeing that many people had arrived according to the signature book, we quietly walked into the first exhibition room. The first impression was that there were too many paintings, too small, arranged too densely, and the labels were too black and too large, obscuring the vividness of the paintings. The second exhibition room was much better. On the east wall, there was a self-portrait of the artist that I liked very much. The simple brushstrokes and thin colors could express the mystery of light and color. That childish smile and that naiveté immediately connected me to her emotionally. If I were not a close friend of the artist, and if I didn't think it was wrong to be a thief, I might have stolen her painting.

There were two hundred pieces by the artist. From these two hundred pieces, one could see the artist's travels and enthusiasms over the years. After returning from France, she visited many famous scenic spots in China. An artist is like a poet or writer. Without traveling thousands of miles and reading thousands of books, there will be no significant gains. I believe that an artist's works are not unrelated to their thoughts, experiences, and environment. I also believe that the achievements of every artist are not accidental but result from considerable experience and hard work.

After seeing Ms. Pan's paintings, I became even more convinced that the achievements of effort have life. The artist's brushstrokes are vigorous while not forgetting delicacy and tenderness, with a grand perspective and attention to detail. She is also skilled in using grayscale colors. We all know that artists are most afraid of using gray because it easily makes paintings dull, but Ms. Pan's skills are skilled and bold, and she can use gray to reflect the vividness of the painting.

Now I want to talk about how Ms. Pan's paintings gave me insight and affection. In many landscape paintings, such as "Welcoming Pine of Huangshan," "Three Hidden Pools of Xuedou Mountain in Fenghua," "Blue Dragon Ridge of Huashan," and "Seashore of Qingdao," the composition is very unique, and the colors and values are bright and dark, making each painting vivid. The pine of Huangshan is majestic, the mountain ridge is towering, and the sea is both calm and turbulent. There is also a painting called "Pine in White Cloud Cave of Laoshan," which is even more serene and grand. The colors of the sky are well painted.

In figure paintings, "Coolie," "Old Prostitute," and "Fugitive" are all full of vitality. Looking at them, it seems that their cells are jumping there. When I saw "Coolie," I unconsciously thought of endurance and hunger. That laborious face, wrinkled and thin, decadent and brave, enduring. He has worked, he has been diligent. The empty basket in his hand and the pipe in his mouth show a little joy and comfort after he has sold his labor. "Fugitive" is also a powerful work. The muscles of the whole body and the expression on the face fully express the melancholy, the struggle of life, and the distress. But "Old Prostitute" shows a disgusting, superficial, boring, shameful, and even chewable soul. That is the gray life. I cannot but admire the artist's mysterious and varied brush. I feel that the artist is not an ordinary artist. She can understand life and penetrate the mind, and she pays attention to everyday life, chewing and savoring it, and always paying attention. After seeing Ms. Pan's paintings, the face of a Russian friend could not help but appear in my mind, that is the face of Lorskaya. Her frankness, liveliness, and hard work are just like Ms. Pan. Lorskaya, because she sympathized with the poor, she roamed in the front gate area of ​​Beijing every day. Sometimes she went to the workers' area to paint the poor, and when she came back, she sculpted in her small studio. I remember that there was a large wooden board with many sculptures on it, all of which were the faces and figures of various coolies. It is said that she has now returned to Russia and has not only become a sculptor but also a painter and a female actor.

I hope that Ms. Pan will not only become a painter, but also a thoughtful writer, because she loves literature very much.

On the Riverside 216

— Shen Jiaqian

In front of my house, there is a vast open space, which is a public land. The neighboring residents each use thin bamboo poles to divide it into their own gardens, planting some seasonal vegetables. In front of the open space is a small river. Because the terrain there is higher, the small river is only knee-deep when the official river is at high tide.
