Don't Forget When You Reach the Main Street 218

— Jasmine

Wife: When you reach the main street, don't forget one thing.

Husband: What thing?

Wife: Go to the Wuzhou Pharmacy to...

Husband: Do what?

Wife: Buy some sanitary products for the house. We're waiting to use them now.

Husband: What sanitary products?

Wife: We need to shower often now, so we can't live without "Wuzhou Eau de Cologne," and "Wuzhou Talcum Powder." Please buy a bottle of each. Also, mosquitoes have been bothering us at night, making it hard to sleep, so please buy a few boxes of "Wuzhou Mosquito Coils." And please buy a few bottles of "Wuzhou Fruit Syrup." Don't forget.

Husband: I definitely won't forget when I reach the main street.

Page 20

We could clearly see the scattered bricks and mud path at the bottom of the creek. At low tide, the rushing water sprayed against the bricks, creating a subtle melody, and the agitated bubbles followed the cracks between the bricks, forming water rings as they flowed into the official river. My companions and I grew up by that small creek. There were stone steps that led directly into the heart of the creek. We would watch the depth of the water and play on the steps. Water was of great interest to every child, and summer was the perfect season. We would sit on the lowest step, our four legs submerged in the heart of the creek, the water splashing against our soles. We even fell asleep on the steps, and by the time we woke up, our lower bodies were completely soaked. But we loved the water. We would secretly change our clothes and continue to watch the sunset on the steps. What made us happiest was when the tide rose, because the creek was narrow. We would weigh down the large manure baskets from the fields with large stones and place them with their mouths facing the incoming tide. The water would flow through the bamboo slits of the baskets, dragging parallel fine lines that disappeared backwards. If the water was rushing, those fine lines would form a beautiful pattern that cannot be described with words. And the small fish and shrimp brought in by the tide would be trapped in the baskets. We would raise those catches in a large vat in the backyard. Within a few days, the fish and shrimp in the vat were quite impressive, so we would spend half of our time visiting them in the backyard every day. When my father discovered this, he praised our intelligence. My father suffered from a severe heart condition, and he followed the doctor's orders to rest quietly in the yard every day, rarely moving around. When he learned about our fishing method in the creek, he would often lean on his cane and have a servant move a rattan chair so he could sit in the open space and watch us playing on the steps. But when my father had to go back inside, he always wanted us to go home with him. However, he knew we hadn't had enough fun, so he would stroke our hair and say with a smile, "Let's go home and have fun!" He was really happy and brought out a glass fish tank, spread stone pebbles for growing daffodils on the bottom, and selected a few more lively fish to raise in it. He spent his time enjoying it every day under the lamp.

My companion was my cousin from my aunt's family. Both my uncle and aunt passed away early, and my father, because she was his sister's flesh and blood, raised her in our home and sent her to school, just like me. But when my cousin entered middle school, it was during the height of the May Fourth Movement. That middle school experienced a major incident, and my cousin disappeared as a result. My father almost fainted because of her. Later, he passed away in grief. On his deathbed, he held my hand and spoke all the words he had stored in his heart: "She is a smart girl. She must have been deceived by someone. She hasn't been heard from for so many years. I'm sorry to your aunt for dying. You must find her!" I originally wanted her to be my wife, but that wish has naturally been dashed. But you must find her!

After my father died, I searched in every direction, but in this vast sea of people, I never found any news of my companion from the creek. For many years, I wandered everywhere, almost forgetting my father's unfulfilled wish. Recently, a neighbor sent me a letter, telling me that the local public land had been bought cheaply by powerful individuals who had devised a way to do so with the local authorities. The small creek has also been filled in, and they are now constructing houses. It is common in my hometown for local bullies and gentry to seize public land and fill in a small creek. Before their final days arrive, their actions can only force us to swallow our anger. But the creek holds my beautiful childhood dreams. My cousin is drifting in who-knows-what place, and now they are building houses on that small creek. This made me think of my father's last words again. I'm afraid his last words will ultimately go unfulfilled.

Straw Bags 219

— Yi Yi

This series of straw shacks is filled with two hundred and eighty-one straw bags.

The young and strong men have all been selected to build highways, leaving only these women, children, and old men who can only eat and are of no use.

Each of them has a hometown, beautiful and fertile fields where their desire for life blossomed. They all shed blood and sweat happily to firmly grasp that living hope, burying their hard labor deep in the fragrant soil, and then drawing a trace of innocent smiles on their tired and taut faces.

Isn't that how it is? Extracting scarce necessities from a large amount of hard work, this is how ancestors have been struggling since long ago. They were faithful to their ancestors' reality, never being lazy and never disobeying the increasingly declining gray "fate." Sometimes, under the weight of life, they felt suffocated, as if grasped tightly by something, but they did overcome this accumulated depression in the joy of working together.

In the past, in the hazy and cool morning mist or bathed in the rose-colored sunset, young and strong couples, children, and old people would smell the fertile and sweet scent of the soil. They were busy, working, and everywhere echoed with bright and pleasant short folk songs, as if they never knew what fatigue was. They were entirely intoxicated in the sacred work.

Like a volcanic eruption, they were thrown far away to a strange foreign land. Then, the past scenes turned into beautiful dreams, fragmented and remaining in the chaotic and turbulent mind without becoming complete.

Now, they have not only lost paradise, but also freedom, and everything...

They are a group of slaves, receiving no sympathy at all. Everything is cold and unfamiliar. Everything in this foreign land seems to have no connection to them, as if it does not welcome this group of guests who have suffered for their "fate." Therefore, they are swirling the common question in their minds: "Who called us to be like this? We used to have homes!..." But this question has never been answered.

"You bastards... straw bags! What use are you? Huh..."

The director shouts like this every time he comes to inspect. He impatiently waves the rattan cane, whipping people, but he always covers his nose with one hand, so he only leaves here hastily for a while to take a deep breath outside.

"Damn it!... No... no... What's the use of living? Grandma's..."

The director seems to be hurt by these straw bags in the straw shacks. Every time, every time, he loses his temper. If there were no straw shacks, he definitely wouldn't have that ugly face.

"Hey, the sorghum is running out again, is it..." The accountant said to the director, "If... we don't pay back a batch of money first, the rice shop won't extend credit anymore!..."

"What are you shouting for? Do you need to be so loud? Damn it! These wastes only know how to eat! Only give each person two small bowls a day... Grandma, wouldn't it be enough if we cooked it a little raw?..."

"Compared to charcoal, firewood... we also need to buy some. Don't put the money..."

"Um... this... this I know... Tsk! There's really no way... really..."

"I heard... I heard that someone from above is coming to check... the accounts, the money, and those things of yours... how, how are we going to explain that?..." The accountant pressed even closer.

"………………"

After a long time, the director slapped his fist on his palm and said:

"Damn it, okay, we'll do it this way..." He walked closer to the accountant and put his mouth close to the accountant's ear. "…………Is that right? Hmm..." He patted the accountant's shoulder: "Hey, buddy! Is there any kindness in this world? Hmm... You get a share!... "

The director smiled, and the accountant smiled too.

Night fell on this desolate wilderness. Some dilapidated mounds lay quietly in the wilderness, without a sound. That series of straw shacks was already blurred in the dim night! Two hundred and eighty-one straw bags breathed out melancholy tunes in lonely dreams. Only in dreams, and only in dreams, did they return to their beautiful hometown and get some comfort that could not be realized.

People of Suzhou (16) 221

— Written by Gu Wenzong

Lilya: After your explanation, I have great doubts about that fancy meal I just had! If that chef isn't from the British Embassy, ​​haven't I been taken for a ride?

Jinghong: That doesn't count as being taken for a ride. Anyway, it's true that your stomach is full. The rest is a matter of what you need psychologically. Because people who like fancy food often like

Lilya: To like French and British food. If you use the terms of French and British food to cater to the psychology of general diners, you will definitely be able to achieve the effect of generating wealth in your business. As for whether the chef on the dining car has worked at the British Embassy, ​​you don’t need to investigate. In fact, you are eating fancy dishes made by Chinese people, but psychologically, you can only tell the difference between British-flavored fancy dishes and Chinese-flavored fancy dishes. What else is there? Why do you feel so upset about this? Anyway, it's fine as long as your stomach is full.

Lilya: I spent so much money on fancy food because I wanted to eat authentic British-flavored fancy food, otherwise, wouldn't I just eat fried rice? Fried rice can also fill you up—really! I'm really a fool among the ordinary people! A country bumpkin! A simpleton! I'm so angry! I'm really too gullible!

Jinghong: Why are you regretting it now? Didn't you just say that people who eat fancy food always eat fancy food? I think a person who eats so-called fancy food must naturally have a big heart. So-called big people eat fancy food, ride in big cars, watch big plays, spend big money, tell big stories, and their hearts must be big, and the situation must be even bigger. Everything is big, isn't it?

National Studies 222

Hu Zhangzhao "Analects—Eight Elegances"

Traffic (1300) 9:30 PM to 10:00 PM

The Master said, "Even among the barbarians, if there is a ruler, it is better than the lack of civilization among the various Xia." The Ji family sacrificed to Mount Tai. The Master said to Ran You, "Can you not save this?" He replied, "I cannot." The Master said, "Alas! Would Mount Tai be less knowledgeable than Lin Fang?" The Master said, "The noble man does not contend for anything. If he must, let it be archery. He bows and yields as they ascend, and drinks as they descend. Their contention is that of noble men."

Zi Xia asked, "With a clever smile and lovely eyes, adorned with plainness, what does it mean?" The Master said, "Painting comes after a plain base." He said, "Is ritual secondary?" The Master said, "It is Shang who inspires me. Now I can speak about poetry with him."

The Master said, "I can speak of the Xia rituals, but Qi is not enough to attest to them. I can speak of the Yin rituals, but Song is not enough to attest to them. It is because the records and wise men are insufficient. If they were sufficient, I could attest to them."

The Master said, "I do not wish to observe the Di sacrifice after the libation has been poured." Someone asked about the explanation of the Di sacrifice. The Master said, "I do not know. He who knows its explanation, in relation to the world, is like showing it here." He pointed to his palm.

Mr. Wang's News 227

Cast Determined: The cast for "The Amazing Adventures of Mr. Wang" has now been completely determined. Mr. Wang, Xiao Chen, Mrs. Wang, and Mrs. Chen will still be played by the original cast members Tang Jie, Cao Xuesong, Sang Shuzhen, and Zhai Qiqi, respectively. However, the role of Little Yuan will be replaced by Li Lin, who is a newcomer to the stage.

Script Approved: The script for "The Amazing Adventures of Mr. Wang" has been officially approved by the 21st examination meeting of the Film Script Examination Committee, and the registration permit was also issued the other day.

Tang Jie Arrives in Shanghai: "Mr. Wang" Tang Jie arrived in Shanghai from Hong Kong on June 1st. That night, he performed with "Xiao Chen" at the Paris Ballroom.

Rushing to Make Costumes: The filming of "The Amazing Adventures of Mr. Wang" is imminent, and three fashion companies are currently designing and rushing to make costumes, extremely busy.

"Peach Blossom Spring Dream" and Half-Naked Women 228

The scenery of mountains and peaks is set up in the photography studio of Xinhua Company. When you get off the tram at Xujiahui, you can vaguely see it in the distance. At the foot of this mountain is the Peach Blossom Village of "Peach Blossom Spring Dream." In a very important scene, not only Han Langen and Liu Jiqun are making a lot of jokes here, but also Tong Yuejuan and Xu Manli appear in strange and bizarre half-naked costumes. Because this "Peach Blossom Village" seems to be in another uncivilized nation, the things worn by the men, women, old, and young there are very few and very thin, and there is a sense of beauty when you are among them. In this way, it is really fun on the screen. It is known that when the stage drama was being filmed, various difficult problems arose. For example, this scene requires seventy young girls. It is not difficult for the theater affairs department to recruit these seventy young girls, but if they are asked to take off their clothes and put on thin gauze, it is not an easy task. Before Xinhua Company started filming this scene of "Peach Blossom Spring Dream," it had considered this point. Originally, it had planned to have seventy girls, and specially asked someone to recruit ninety, preparing for the possibility that twenty girls would refuse to take off their clothes. As a result, among these ninety girls, as many as forty expressed their unwillingness and returned, leaving fifty girls to complete this unique and aesthetically pleasing scene.

Chen Juanjuan Officially Joins Xinhua Company 229

Chen Juanjuan appeared on the screen as a nine-year-old girl, but her achievements are no less than those of "big children." Among the child stars in China, Chen Juanjuan is of course the best. Now, Chen Juanjuan and her mother-in-law both feel that filming one film here and one film there is unstable. Starting in June, she officially joined Xinhua Company and became a basic actor of Xinhua. Xinhua has great hopes for Chen Juanjuan and has entrusted a "major screenwriter" to write a script specifically for this child.

"The Glamour of the Singing World" Biographical Notes 230

The film is scheduled to be released today at the Great Light

The song and dance epic "The Singing Kid" starring Al Jolson is scheduled to be released today (Friday) at the Great Light. Because Al Jolson is a meritorious official of Warner Bros., the company has spent a lot of money on the film he stars in, and the supporting actors are also particularly valued. In addition to Al Jolson, the film also features Beverly Roberts, a newcomer to the scene in 1936, baby star Sybil Gibson, comedian Edward Horton, and Alan Dinehart, who play minor roles in the play, making it even more beautiful. In the singing part, the famous band leader Kyle Carroll and his "Hot Band", and the four famous singers of the American Yacht Club have joined hands to cooperate. There is not much dialogue in the film. The entire atmosphere vibrates between the fast-paced singing and dancing shadows. In short, this "Glamour of the Singing World" can be called a supreme entertainment musical dance drama.
